Creation of Servants and Divine Sovereignty
Sanusi denies divine obligation in creation and actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Sunni doctrine, nothing is obligatory upon God in His actions, including the creation of human actions and reward/punishment.

Core Idea
God is sovereign over all actions; nothing is obligatory upon Him.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a critical point of theological dispute: whether God is obligated to create what is best for His servants. The Mu'tazila argued for such an obligation, but Sanusi affirms the Ash'ari position that God's actions are not constrained by any external obligation. This lesson unpacks the implications of divine sovereignty for human actions, reward, and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note key terms like 'ja'iz' (permissible) and 'la yajibu' (not obligatory).
The passage begins with 'Mina al-ja'izat'...
2
Identify the central claim
Find where Sanusi states that nothing is obligatory upon God. Understand why this contrasts with the Mu'tazila position.
The last sentence calls this the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider how this doctrine preserves divine transcendence and the purpose of trial and tribulation.
If God were obligated to create the best, there would be no test.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في خلق العباد وأفعالهم ومايتعلق بذلك
ومِنَ الجائزاتِ في حقِّهِ تعالى : خَلْقُ العباد ، وخلق أعمالهم ، وخلْقُ الثواب والعقاب عليها ، لا يجب عليهِ مِنْ ذلكَ ، ولا مراعاة صلاح ولا أصلح ، وإلا وجبَ ألا يكون تكليف ولا محنة دنيويَّةٌ ولا أخرويَّةٌ ، والأفعالُ كلُّها ؛ خيرُها وشرها ، نفعُها وضرُّها . . مستوية في الدلالة على باهر قدرتِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ وسعة علمه ونفوذ إرادته ، لا يتطرَّقُ لذاتِهِ العليَّةِ مِنْ ذلكَ كمال ولا نقص .
كانَ اللهُ ولا شيء معَهُ ، وهو الآن على ما كان عليه ، فأكرم سبحانَهُ مَنْ شاءَ بما لا يُكيَّفُ مِنْ أنواع النعيمِ بمجرَّدِ فضله ، لا لميل إليه ، أو قضاء حقٌّ وجبَ لَهُ عليهِ ، وعدل فيمَنْ شاءَ بما لا يُطاقُ وصفُهُ مِنْ أصناف الجحيم ،
لا لإشفاء غيظ ولا لضررٍ نالَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِهِ
•
ممَّا يجب على كلِّ مُكلَّفٍ أَنْ يعتقدَهُ : أَنَّ أَفعال الله سبحانه وتعالى ؛ ذواتاً كانَتْ أو أعراضاً ، كان فيها صلاح للعبادِ أو لم يكن .. لا يجب عليه منها شيء ، هذا مذهب أهل الحق
Chapter
On the creation of servants and their actions and what pertains to that
And among the permissible things with respect to Him, exalted, are: the creation of servants, the creation of their actions, and the creation of reward and punishment upon them. Nothing of that is obligatory upon Him, nor is consideration of well-being or what is more beneficial. Otherwise, there would necessarily be no trial (taklif) and no worldly or otherworldly tribulation. And all actions—their good and evil, their benefit and harm—are equal in indicating His overwhelming power, the breadth of His knowledge, and the penetration of His will. No perfection or deficiency attaches to His sublime essence from any of that.
God existed when there was nothing with Him, and He is now as He was. So He honored whom He willed with kinds of bliss that cannot be qualified, solely by His grace—not due to inclination toward them, nor fulfillment of a right that became obligatory upon Him. And He dealt justly with whom He willed with types of hellfire that cannot be described—not to vent anger, nor because of harm that reached Him from them.
Among what every legally responsible person must believe: that the actions of God, whether they are substances or accidents, whether they involve benefit for the servants or not, nothing of them is obligatory upon Him. This is the doctrine of the people of truth.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement (or a short chapter) on God's creation of human beings and their actions, and the related issues of reward, punishment, and divine obligation. It first declares that it is permissible (ja'iz) for God to create servants, their actions, and the reward and punishment for those actions. Nothing of this is obligatory upon Him—including any consideration of what is beneficial (salah) or most beneficial (aslah). If God were obligated to create what is best, then there would be no purpose for trial, tribulation, or test in this world or the next. The passage then emphasizes that all actions—good and evil, beneficial and harmful—are equal in indicating God's overwhelming power, knowledge, and will; none of them adds perfection or deficiency to His essence. Next, it affirms God's eternal existence alone, and His unchanged state now. It explains that God honors whom He wills with indescribable bliss solely by His grace, not because of any inclination or obligation. Similarly, He punishes whom He wills with indescribable torment, not out of anger or because of harm from them. Finally, it states that every legally responsible person (mukallaf) must believe that none of God's actions—whether they are substances or accidents, and whether they benefit people or not—are obligatory upon Him. This is identified as the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth), in contrast to the Mu'tazila who held that God must create what is best for His servants (aslah).

Key Terms
خلق العباد
جائز
صلاح
أصلح
تكليف
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God is obligated to create what is best for His servants (aslah).
Correction: This passage affirms that nothing is obligatory upon God; His actions are purely by His wisdom and will.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what must a Muslim believe about God's actions?
A) God must always create what is best for His servants
B) God is obligated to reward the obedient and punish the disobedient
C) Nothing is obligatory upon God in any of His actions
D) God's actions are limited by His attributes

Key Takeaway
The belief that nothing is obligatory upon God in His actions is a fundamental tenet of Sunni theology, distinguishing it from the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself thinking that God owes you something because of your prayers, charity, or obedience? How does this lesson's claim that nothing is obligatory upon God challenge that entitlement? What should your attitude become instead?
?
When you face hardship or see others suffering, do you sometimes feel that God is being unfair? How does the statement that all actions—good and evil, benefit and harm—are equal in pointing to God's power, and that He does not punish out of anger, reshape your understanding of trials? Will you trust His wisdom even when you don't understand?
?
This lesson says God honored some and punished others solely by His will, not because of any obligation. If your salvation depends entirely on His unconstrained grace, what does that mean for your pride in your deeds? How will you live today in response to this radical dependence on His mercy?

Divine Attributes

No Obligation on God in His Actions
Sanusi enumerates possible divine acts and negates any obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Ash'ari theology, nothing is obligatory upon God in His actions, including creating servants, their deeds, and reward/punishment.

Core Idea
God's actions are not obligatory; they flow from His will, not from necessity.

In this passage, Imam al-Sanusi lays out the foundational Ash'ari principle that God is not bound by any obligation in His actions. He lists the kinds of acts that are possible for God and then emphatically states that none of them are required of Him. This sets the stage for understanding divine absolute sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of Sanusi.
2
Identify the list of possible actions
Find the enumerated actions listed as possible (jā'izāt) for God. Notice they include creation of servants, their actions, and reward/punishment.
These are examples of what God can do, not what He must do.
3
Understand the negation of obligation
Focus on the phrase 'la yajibu 'alayhi min dhalika' (nothing of that is obligatory upon Him). This is the core claim.
4
Examine the consequence if obligation were true
The passage argues that if any act were obligatory, it would negate the very concept of divine testing (taklīf and miḥna). Understand this logical consequence.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
5
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider why this principle is crucial for maintaining God's absolute sovereignty and freedom from external compulsion.
This distinguishes Ash'ari from Mu'tazili thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في خلق العباد وأفعالهم ومايتعلق بذلك
ومِنَ الجائزاتِ في حقَّهِ تعالى : خَلْقُ العباد ، وخلق أعمالهم ، وخلْقُ الثواب والعقاب عليها ، لا يجب عليهِ مِنْ ذلكَ ، ولا مراعاة صلاح ولا أصلح ، وإلا وجبَ ألا يكون تكليف ولا محنة دنيويَّةٌ ولا أخرويَّةٌ ، والأفعالُ كلُّها ؛ خيرُها وشرها ، نفعُها وضرُّها . . مستوية في الدلالة على باهر قدرتِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ وسعة علمه ونفوذ إرادته ، لا يتطرَّقُ لذاتِهِ العليَّةِ مِنْ ذلكَ كمال ولا نقص .
كانَ اللهُ ولا شيء معَهُ ، وهو الآن على ما كان عليه ، فأكرم سبحانَهُ مَنْ شاءَ بما لا يُكيَّفُ مِنْ أنواع النعيمِ بمجرَّدِ فضله ، لا لميل إليه ، أو قضاء حقٌّ وجبَ لَهُ عليهِ ، وعدل فيمَنْ شاءَ بما لا يُطاقُ وصفُهُ مِنْ أصناف الجحيم ،
لا لإشفاء غيظ ولا لضررٍ نالَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِهِ
•
ممَّا يجب على كلِّ مُكلَّفٍ أَنْ يعتقدَهُ : أَنَّ أَفعال الله سبحانه وتعالى ؛ ذواتاً كانَتْ أو أعراضاً ، كان فيها صلاح للعبادِ أو لم يكن .. لا يجب عليه منها شيء ، هذا مذهب أهل الحق
Section: On the creation of servants and their actions and what pertains to that. Among the possible things in His right – exalted is He – are: the creation of servants, the creation of their actions, and the creation of reward and punishment upon them. Nothing of that is obligatory upon Him, nor is consideration of what is beneficial or most beneficial [obligatory]; otherwise it would be necessary that there be no obligation (taklīf) and no worldly or otherworldly trial. And all actions – their good and their evil, their benefit and their harm – are equal in indicating His overwhelming power – may He be glorified and exalted – and the vastness of His knowledge and the penetration of His will. Neither perfection nor deficiency attaches to His sublime essence from any of that. God was and nothing was with Him, and He is now as He was. So He honors – glorified is He – whom He wills with types of bliss that cannot be qualified, by mere grace, not due to inclination toward them, nor as fulfillment of a right that was due to him from Him; and He is just toward whom He wills with types of hellfire whose description cannot be endured, not to satisfy anger nor due to harm that came to Him from him. From what is obligatory upon every morally responsible person to believe: that the actions of God – glorified and exalted is He – whether essences or accidents, whether they contain benefit for the servants or not – nothing of them is obligatory upon Him. This is the doctrine of the people of truth.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement of the Ash'ari position regarding divine acts. The author begins by listing what is possible for God: creating servants, their actions, and the reward and punishment upon them, while emphasizing that none of these are obligatory upon Him. He then argues that if any act were obligatory, it would entail the necessity of there being no trial or obligation, which contradicts the reality of divine testing. All actions, both good and evil, are equal in manifesting God's power, knowledge, and will; they add neither perfection nor deficiency to His essence. The author then presents a classic Ash'ari principle: 'God was and nothing was with Him, and He is now as He was,' meaning His attributes and actions are eternal, and He remains unchanged. God's rewarding and punishing are purely by His grace and justice, not due to any external cause. The passage concludes with a summary of the essential belief: none of God's actions, whether they involve created essences or accidents, are obligatory upon Him, regardless of whether they benefit the servants. This is the doctrine of ahl al-haqq (the people of truth, i.e., the Ash'aris).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God is obligated to do what is best for humanity.
Correction: The Ash'ari position is that God is not obligated to do anything; His actions are purely by will, and 'best' is not a standard binding on Him.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if something were obligatory on God, what would necessarily be absent?
A) The creation of servants
B) Obligation (taklīf) and trial (miḥna)
C) Reward and punishment
D) Divine power

Key Takeaway
God's actions are all possible, and nothing is obligatory upon Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel entitled to God's mercy or reward? This passage says nothing is obligatory upon God. How does that confront your expectation of being treated fairly? Will you still worship Him even if He does not 'owe' you anything?
?
The passage mentions worldly and otherworldly trial. Are you willing to accept trials without feeling that God is being unjust? Can you submit to His freedom to test you however He wills?
?
If God's actions are not constrained by what we consider beneficial, then His wisdom may be beyond our understanding. Are you ready to trust His choices even when they seem harmful to you? What would it take for you to surrender that last bit of control?

The Equality of Actions in Manifesting God's Power and His Unchanging Nature
Sanusi asserts the equality of actions and God's unchangeable nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all actions, good and evil, equally demonstrate God's power and that His essence is unaffected by them, and that His rewarding and punishing are purely by grace and justice.

Core Idea
All actions are equal in showing God's power; He remains unchanged and acts by will.

This passage continues the discussion by emphasizing that no action adds or subtracts from God's perfection. All deeds, regardless of their moral or practical value, are equal in pointing to His overwhelming power. The text then presents the timeless nature of God and the basis for reward and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the poetic phrasing 'kāna Allāhu wa lā shay'a ma'ahu'.
2
Understand the equality of actions
Note that Sanusi says all actions, good and evil, beneficial and harmful, are 'equal' (mustawiya) in indicating God's power. This means no act is more or less indicative of divine attributes.
This refutes the idea that evil acts somehow detract from God's majesty.
3
Connect equality to divine transcendence
Realize that because actions are equal in indicating power, they do not affect God's essence: neither perfection nor deficiency attaches to Him from any action.
God's essence is utterly transcendent and beyond the reach of creation.
4
Reflect on God's eternal nature
The statement 'God was and nothing was with Him, and He is now as He was' affirms God's self-sufficiency and immutability. Consider how this supports the non-obligation principle.
God does not change or acquire new attributes through creation.
5
Analyze the basis for reward and punishment
Sanusi explains that God honors by mere grace, not due to any right or inclination, and punishes by justice, not anger or harm. This reinforces that rewards and punishments are not obligatory but purely voluntary acts of God.

Among the possible things in His right – exalted is He – are: the creation of servants, the creation of their actions, and the creation of reward and punishment upon them. Correction: The passage states that neither perfection nor deficiency attaches to God from any action; He is utterly transcendent and unaffected.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for God's honoring whom He wills?
A) Because of a right due from God
B) By mere grace without inclination or due right
C) Because of the servant's merit
D) To satisfy anger

Key Takeaway
God's actions are all equal in manifesting His power, and He remains unchanged; reward and punishment are purely by His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you receive a blessing, do you feel you deserve it? The passage says reward is by mere grace, not due to any right. Search your heart: do you truly believe that your good deeds could never obligate God to reward you? If so, how would that change your gratitude and humility today?
?
When you see evil or suffering in the world, do you doubt God's goodness or question His justice? The passage declares that all actions are equal in indicating His power and no deficiency attaches to Him. Can you still trust that God is perfectly just even when you don't understand His decree? What would it mean for you to surrender that question to His unchangeable wisdom?
?
The text affirms that God was and nothing was with Him, and He is now as He was. This means nothing ever changes His essence or obligates Him. Does your relationship with God rest on the belief that He is unchangeably good, or do you sometimes act as if your behavior can sway Him? What would it look like to live today with the certainty that God's grace and justice are not reactions to your actions but flow from His eternal will?

beginner
3 min
The Three Brothers Scenario
Sanusi states the three-part scenario and initial Mu'tazilite response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial scenario and the Mu'tazilite position on the fates of three persons.

Core Idea
Three fates expose the Mu'tazilite doctrine to logical testing.

Sanusi presents a famous dialectical encounter between Imam al-Ash'ari and his Mu'tazilite teacher al-Jubba'i. The scenario of three brothers—a child, an adult unbeliever, and an adult believer—is set up to test the Mu'tazilite principle that Allah must always do what is most beneficial (al-aslah). This lesson covers the initial question and al-Jubba'i's straightforward answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the scenario
Read the Arabic passage describing the three persons and their fates as stated by al-Jubba'i.
Notice the precise classification: the child is in Paradise, the adult unbeliever in Hell, the adult believer in the highest ranks.
2
Understand the Mu'tazilite premise
Recall that the Mu'tazilites believe Allah is obligated to do what is most beneficial for His creatures. Al-Jubba'i's answers reflect this principle.
3
Identify the initial question
Observe that al-Ash'ari's first question is deceptively simple. It sets the stage for the logical trap.
The real challenge comes in the next lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح ! فقالَ الشيخُ للجبائي : ما تقولُ في ثلاثة أشخاص : مات أحدهم قبل البلوغ ، والآخر مات بعد البلوغ كافراً ، والآخرُ ماتَ بعدَهُ مؤمناً ؟
فقال الجبائيُّ : أمَّا الصغيرُ ففي الجنَّةِ ، وأمَّا الكافرُ الكبير ففي النارِ ، وأمَّا الكبيرُ المؤمنُ ففي الدرجاتِ العُلا
فقال له الشيخ : ما بال الصغيرِ قُصِرَ بهِ عن درجاتِ الكبير المؤمن ؟ فقالَ الجبائي : لأنَّه لم يعمل قدر عملِهِ
فقالَ لهُ الشيخُ : مِنْ حُجَّتِهِ على مذهبكم أن يقول : يا ربِّ ؛ كانَ الأصلح في حقي أن تكون أبقيتني حيّاً حتى أصل بالعمل الدرجة العليا
فقال الجبائي : جوابُهُ : أنْ يقولَ اللهُ تعالى له : علمتُ أنَّكُ لو بقيت إلى سنّ التكليف لكفرْتَ ، فتُخلَّدُ في النار ، فالأصلحُ في حقك موتُكَ صغيراً كما فعلْتُ بكَ ؛ لسلامتِكَ بِهِ مِنَ الخلودِ في النار التي هي مِنْ أعظم غنيمةٍ ، فكيف وقد زدتكَ على ذلكَ ما لا يُكَيَّفُ مِنْ نعيمِ الجنَّةِ ؟ !
فقالَ لهُ الشيخُ : فإذاً يقومُ الثالثُ الذي مات كبيراً كافراً بل وكلُّ كافِرٍ مِنْ دَرَكاتِ لظى فيقولُ : يا ربِّ ؛ كنا نرضى منكَ بأدنى مِنْ مرتبةِ [؟] فما لنا هذا الصبي نالم تمثنا صغاراً قبل التكليف وقد علمتَ منَّا الكفرَ بعده كما فعلت بهذا الصبي ؟!
فبُهِتَ الجبائي ، ولم يَقدِرْ أنْ يجيب بكلمةٍ
فقالَ لهُ الشيخُ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : وقفَ حمارُ الشيخ في العقبة
ثم قالَ : تعالى أنْ تُوزَنَ أحكامُ ذي الجلال بميزان الاعتزال
Regarding the consideration of what is most fitting and better! So the Shaykh said to al-Jubba'i: What do you say about three persons: one died before puberty, another died after puberty as an unbeliever, and another died after it as a believer? Al-Jubba'i said: As for the child, he is in Paradise; as for the adult unbeliever, he is in the Fire; and as for the adult believer, he is in the highest ranks. The Shaykh said to him: Why is the child restricted from the ranks of the adult believer? Al-Jubba'i said: Because he did not do deeds equal to his deeds. The Shaykh said to him: From his argument according to your school is that he says: O my Lord, what was most fitting for me was that You keep me alive so that I might attain the highest rank through deeds. Al-Jubba'i said: The answer to him is that Allah Almighty says to him: I knew that if you remained until the age of obligation you would disbelieve and thus be eternally in the Fire, so what was most fitting for you was your death as a child, as I did with you, for your safety from eternal damnation in the Fire, which is among the greatest gains. Moreover, I have added for you beyond that an unquantifiable delight of Paradise! The Shaykh said to him: Then the third one who died as an adult unbeliever, indeed every unbeliever from the depths of Hellfire, stands up and says: O Lord, we would be content with You with something less than the rank of [?] So why is it that we have this child? [unclear] we were made children before obligation while You knew from us disbelief after it, just as You did with this child? So al-Jubba'i was stunned and was unable to answer a word. The Shaykh, may Allah be pleased with him, said to him: The Shaykh's donkey got stuck in the pass. Then he said: Exalted is He that the judgments of the Majestic should be weighed by the scale of Mu'tazilism.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage is a theological refutation presented as a narrative. It recounts a famous debate between Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (the Shaykh) and his Mu'tazilite teacher al-Jubba'i concerning the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah, which holds that Allah must always do what is most fitting and beneficial for His creatures. Al-Ash'ari poses a scenario of three persons to expose a logical contradiction in this doctrine.

The scenario: one dies before puberty (innocent), one dies as an adult unbeliever, and one dies as an adult believer. Al-Jubba'i states their fates: the child in Paradise, the unbeliever in Hell, and the believer in the highest ranks. Al-Ash'ari then asks why the child is at a lower rank than the believer. Al-Jubba'i replies that it is because the child did not perform deeds. Al-Ash'ari then puts forward an objection from the child's perspective: if al-aslah requires that Allah do what is most beneficial, then it would have been better for the child to have been kept alive to perform deeds and attain the higher rank. Al-Jubba'i answers by saying that Allah knew that if the child had reached the age of obligation, he would have disbelieved and been eternally punished, so death in childhood was actually more beneficial to him, sparing him from Hell and granting him Paradise.

Al-Ash'ari then counters by introducing the third person, the adult unbeliever. He argues that according to al-Jubba'i's reasoning, the adult unbeliever can now complain: 'O Lord, why did You not make me die as a child as well, since You knew I would disbelieve? That would have been more beneficial for me, sparing me from Hell and giving me Paradise.' This objection leaves al-Jubba'i speechless. Al-Ash'ari concludes with a witty remark ('the Shaykh's donkey got stuck') and declares that the judgments of Allah cannot be weighed by the scale of Mu'tazilism, implying that human reason cannot dictate what Allah must do.

Key Terms
الصلاح والأصلح
الجبائي
الشيخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah is consistent with ordinary Islamic beliefs about reward and punishment.
Correction: This scenario will show that al-aslah leads to contradictions when applied consistently.

Checkpoint
In the scenario, what is the fate of the adult believer according to al-Jubba'i?
A) He is in Paradise, but at a lower rank than the child.
B) He is in the highest ranks.
C) He is in Hell.
D) He is in a state of waiting.

Key Takeaway
The three brothers scenario sets up a test of the Mu'tazilite principle that Allah must always do what is most beneficial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the three fates, did any part of you feel that the adult unbeliever's fate was too harsh, or the child's fate too lenient? What does that reaction tell you about your own expectations of divine justice vs. what the text presents?
?
Al-Jubba'i's answer places the child in Paradise without merit. Do you believe that God's mercy can override 'fairness' in that way? How does this challenge your personal sense of what is 'just'?
?
The passage begins with the principle of al-aslah (what is most fitting). Have you ever blamed God for not giving you what you thought was 'best'? What might this scenario teach you about the limits of human judgment regarding God's actions?

The Child's Objection to al-Aslah
Sanusi presents the child's objection and al-Jubba'i's answer using divine foreknowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the child's objection that al-aslah would require keeping him alive for greater reward, and al-Jubba'i's counter using divine foreknowledge.

Core Idea
Divine foreknowledge can justify apparent inequalities in al-aslah.

Al-Ash'ari now presses the logical implications of al-aslah. If Allah must do what is most beneficial, why was the child not kept alive to earn a higher rank? Al-Jubba'i responds by invoking Allah's knowledge that the child would have disbelieved, making death in childhood actually more beneficial. This lesson examines that exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the child's objection
Read the Arabic where al-Ash'ari raises the objection from the child's perspective: why was he not kept alive to attain higher rank?
This objection is based on the Mu'tazilite own principle: al-aslah.
2
Read al-Jubba'i's answer
Al-Jubba'i uses divine foreknowledge: Allah knew the child would disbelieve, so death as a child is actually more beneficial.
Note the reasoning: safety from eternal Hellfire is a great gain.
3
Identify the logic
Notice that al-Jubba'i's answer relies on Allah's knowledge of the future. This will be turned against him in the next lesson.
The argument now hinges on how Allah's knowledge is used.

Checkpoint
According to al-Jubba'i, why was it actually more beneficial for the child to die early?
A) Because the child would have been a great sinner if he lived.
B) Because Allah knew the child would disbelieve, sparing him Hell.
C) Because the child would have become a believer anyway.
D) Because the child's death allowed him to enter Paradise earlier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The child receives bliss without earning it because God prevented him from sinning. If you were in that child's position, would you be satisfied with God's plan? What does that reveal about your trust in divine wisdom?
?
Al-Jubba'i argues that early death is better because it prevents eternal punishment. If you truly believed that dying young could save you from future sins, would you welcome death? What does that say about your attachment to this life?

The Adult Unbeliever's Counter-Objection
Sanusi presents the adult unbeliever's objection and al-Ash'ari's concluding rebuke.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses the adult unbeliever's complaint to expose a logical contradiction in the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari turns al-Jubba'i's own logic against him, leaving him speechless.

Al-Ash'ari now springs the trap. If Allah's foreknowledge of disbelief justifies causing an early death for the child's benefit, then the same reasoning should apply to the adult unbeliever. Why was he not made to die as a child? Al-Jubba'i has no answer. This lesson captures the final refutation and al-Ash'ari's powerful conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the adult unbeliever's complaint
Read the Arabic where the adult unbeliever argues that he should have been killed as a child to be spared Hell.
This directly mirrors the logic al-Jubba'i used for the child.
2
Observe al-Jubba'i's silence
Note that al-Jubba'i is stunned and cannot reply. This shows the force of the objection.
The phrase 'the Shaykh's donkey got stuck' is a witty metaphor for a dead end.
3
Understand the conclusion
Al-Ash'ari declares that Allah's judgments cannot be weighed by human scales like Mu'tazilism.
This refutes the very basis of al-aslah: human reason cannot dictate what Allah must do.

This passage is a theological refutation presented as a narrative. It recounts a famous debate between Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (the Shaykh) and his Mu'tazilite teacher al-Jubba'i concerning the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah, which holds that Allah must always do what is most fitting and beneficial for His creatures. Al-Ash'ari poses a scenario of three persons to expose a logical contradiction in this doctrine.

The scenario: one dies before puberty (innocent), one dies as an adult unbeliever, and one dies as an adult believer. Al-Jubba'i states their fates: the child in Paradise, the unbeliever in Hell, and the believer in the highest ranks. Al-Ash'ari then asks why the child is at a lower rank than the believer. Al-Jubba'i replies that it is because the child did not perform deeds. Al-Ash'ari then puts forward an objection from the child's perspective: if al-aslah requires that Allah do what is most beneficial, then it would have been better for the child to have been kept alive to perform deeds and attain the higher rank. Al-Jubba'i answers by saying that Allah knew that if the child had reached the age of obligation, he would have disbelieved and been eternally punished, so death in childhood was actually more beneficial to him, sparing him from Hell and granting him Paradise.

Al-Ash'ari then counters by introducing the third person, the adult unbeliever. He argues that according to al-Jubba'i's reasoning, the adult unbeliever can now complain: 'O Lord, why did You not make me die as a child as well, since You knew I would disbelieve? That would have been more beneficial for me, sparing me from Hell and giving me Paradise.' This objection leaves al-Jubba'i speechless. Al-Ash'ari concludes with a witty remark ('the Shaykh's donkey got stuck') and declares that the judgments of Allah cannot be weighed by the scale of Mu'tazilism, implying that human reason cannot dictate what Allah must do.

Key Terms
الخلود في النار
ميزان الاعتزال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's objection is just rhetoric and does not refute the Mu'tazilite position.
Correction: The objection is a logical reduction ad absurdum: if al-Jubba'i's answer is accepted, it leads to a clear contradiction that cannot be resolved within Mu'tazilite premises.

Checkpoint
Why is al-Jubba'i unable to answer al-Ash'ari's final objection?
A) Because he forgot the argument.
B) Because the objection shows a logical contradiction in his own position.
C) Because he was afraid of al-Ash'ari.
D) Because the adult unbeliever's complaint is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari refutes the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah by showing that it leads to an absurd conclusion when applied consistently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where God's decree seems unfair to you, do you trust His wisdom or do you feel entitled to an explanation? How does al-Ash'ari's rebuke reshape your attitude toward divine judgments?
?
Al-Jubba'i was silenced because he insisted on measuring God's actions by human standards. In what areas of your life have you done the same, expecting God to act according to your sense of fairness? What would it take for you to submit to God's absolute sovereignty, even when His judgments seem incomprehensible?
?
The adult unbeliever's hypothetical objection exposes the fallacy of believing that God owes us anything. Do you secretly hold a sense of entitlement before God? What specific expectation of God's treatment of you does this passage challenge you to surrender?

Transmitted Proofs: Actions as Signs, Not Causes
Sanusi presents transmitted proofs and explains the doctrine of actions as signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari theology holds that actions are not rational causes for reward or punishment, and how transmitted proofs support this doctrine.

Core Idea
Actions are signs, not causes, of divine reward and punishment.

Sanusi now turns to transmitted evidence — Qur'an and hadith — to support the Ash'ari position that actions do not inherently cause reward or punishment. He cites two key verses and a prophetic tradition, then explains the rational principle behind them. This lesson unpacks that evidence and connects it to the broader doctrine of divine sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qur'anic proofs
Read the two verses cited: 'He is not questioned about what He does' (21:23) and 'If your Lord had willed, He would have made the people one community' (11:118). Note how they establish Allah's absolute sovereignty and freedom from human standards of justice.
These verses are foundational for Ash'ari arguments against Mu'tazilite rationalism.
2
Understand the rational principle
The explanation states that all actions are equal in relation to Allah; reward and punishment are purely by His grace or justice, not by any intrinsic merit in the acts themselves.
This is the core of the Ash'ari view: no action compels divine response.
3
Analyze the hadith about surplus
Read the report that Allah creates people for the surplus of Paradise and Fire without prior deeds. This reinforces that divine will is the sole determinant of ultimate destiny.
This affirms that salvation and damnation are not earned by actions alone.
4
Check your understanding
Take the checkpoint quiz to confirm you can distinguish signs from causes and explain why actions are called 'recompense' only conventionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا المنقولُ : فقولُهُ تعالى : ﴿ لَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ وَهُمْ يُسْأَلُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٣] ، وكقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَجَعَلَ النَّاسَ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً﴾ [هود : ١١٨] ، ونحو ذلك ممَّا هو كثير .
قوله : ( فأكرمَ سبحانَهُ مَنْ شاءَ. ) إلى آخرِهِ : يشير إلى أنَّ الأعمال ليسَتْ علَّةً عقليةً لاستحقاق ثواب ولا عقاب ؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ وجوب استواء الأفعالِ كلّها بالنسبة إليهِ تعالى ، وما أُثيبَ عليه منها أو عُوقب فهو بمحض فضلِهِ تعالى أو عدلِهِ ، وإِنَّما الأفعال علامات مخلوقة الله تعالى ، بيَّنَ الشرعُ ما اختار الله سبحانَهُ أَنْ تدلَّ عليهِ مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يكونَ بينَهما ربط عقلي ، وتسمية الثواب والعقاب جزاءً ؛ لأنَّهما في صورة الجزاء ؛ لسبق ما يدل عليه شرعاً
وقد وردَ : أَنَّهُ سبحانه يخلقُ لفضلة النارِ قوماً يُعذِّبُهم ولفضلةِ الجنَّةِ قوماً يُنعمُهم بها مِنْ غيرِ أن يسبق عمل للفريقين .
As for the transmitted evidence: His saying, the Most High: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned' [al-Anbiya': 23], and like His saying, the Most High: 'And if your Lord had willed, He would have made the people one community' [Hud: 118], and similar to that which is abundant. His saying: (So He honored, glorified be He, whom He willed...) to its end: indicates that actions are not a rational cause for deserving reward or punishment; because you know of the necessity of the equality of all actions in relation to Him, the Most High. And whatever is rewarded or punished among them is purely by His grace or His justice. Actions are only created signs of Allah, the Most High. The Law has clarified what Allah, glorified be He, chose that they should indicate, without there being a rational connection between them. The naming of reward and punishment as 'recompense' is because they are in the form of recompense, due to the prior indication of the Law. And it has been reported that He, glorified be He, creates for the surplus of the Fire a people whom He punishes, and for the surplus of Paradise a people whom He delights, without any deed preceding from either group.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a combined argument from transmitted revelation (Qur'an and hadith) and rational explanation to refute the idea that actions are rational causes for reward or punishment. The author first cites two Qur'anic verses: 'He is not questioned about what He does' (21:23), which establishes Allah's absolute sovereignty and that His actions are not subject to human scrutiny; and 'If your Lord had willed, He would have made the people one community' (11:118), which shows that divine will is not constrained by human notions of justice. These verses support the Ash'ari position that actions have no inherent causal efficacy in determining reward or punishment.

The author then explains a previous statement (from the commentary on the text) that actions are not rational causes for deserving reward or punishment. The reason given is the Ash'ari principle that all actions are equal in relation to Allah; they have no intrinsic moral quality that necessitates a particular divine response. Instead, reward and punishment are purely based on Allah's grace (for the obedient) or His justice (for the disobedient), and are not compelled by the actions themselves. Actions are described as 'created signs' that Allah has made to indicate, through revelation, which deeds lead to reward and which to punishment. There is no rational (causal) connection between the act and its consequence; it is purely by divine appointment. The term 'recompense' is used conventionally because the sequence of action and consequence resembles a cause-effect relationship, but it is not based on inherent merit.

The passage concludes with a reported hadith (or tradition) that Allah creates people specifically for the surplus of Paradise or Hell, without any prior deeds from them. This underscores the Ash'ari view that salvation and damnation are ultimately dependent on Allah's will and decree, not on human effort alone. This refutes the Mu'tazilite position that human actions rationally determine reward and punishment.

عدل
علامات مخلوقة
ربط عقلي
فضلة النار
فضلة الجنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Actions are independent causes that compel God to reward or punish based on their intrinsic merit.
Correction: Actions have no inherent causal power; they are only signs. Reward and punishment are purely by Allah's will, based on His grace or justice, not on any necessity from the acts.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are actions considered 'signs' rather than causes of reward and punishment?
A) Because actions have no connection whatsoever to reward or punishment.
B) Because people cannot know which actions are good or bad without revelation.
C) Because all actions are equal in relation to Allah, and He assigns reward or punishment purely by His will.
D) Because reward and punishment are based solely on faith, not deeds.

Key Takeaway
Actions are divinely appointed signs, not independent causes; reward and punishment are solely by Allah's grace and justice, rooted in His will, not in any intrinsic merit of the acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though your deeds are only signs that Allah uses to display His grace and justice, or do you secretly believe that you deserve reward because of your actions? How does this belief affect your relationship with Allah when you fall short?
?
If your ultimate destiny in Paradise or the Fire is ultimately determined by Allah's will and not solely by your deeds, does that make you more humble or more anxious? Why?
?
When you see others who are less religious, do you judge them as if their actions ought to bring punishment, forgetting that the connection is only by divine appointment? What does this say about your view of Allah's sovereignty?

Actions Are Signs, Not Rational Causes
Sanusi states the core claim and its reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari theology holds that actions are not rational causes for reward or punishment, but rather signs created by Allah that indicate His will through revelation.

Core Idea
Actions do not inherently deserve reward or punishment; they are signs of divine will.

Sanusi begins by clarifying a crucial point in Ash'ari theology: actions are not rational causes (علة عقلية) that obligate reward or punishment. Instead, they are created signs that point to what Allah has decreed. This refutes the Mu'tazili notion of inherent moral qualities in acts. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this foundational claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the Arabic passage once, focusing on the phrase 'actions are not rational causes'. Then read the translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the emphasis on equality of all actions before Allah.
2
Identify the core claim and its basis
The passage states that actions are not rational causes because all actions are equal in relation to Allah. Reward or punishment is purely by His grace or justice.
3
Understand the alternative: actions as signs
Instead of rational causes, actions are 'created signs' (علامات مخلوقة). The Law (shar‘) clarifies what each action indicates, with no rational connection.
4
Note the metaphorical use of 'recompense'
The terms 'reward' and 'punishment' are called recompense only because they follow a prior revealed indication, not because of any inherent necessity.
This shows the conventional nature of the link.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فأكرمَ سبحانَهُ مَنْ شاءَ. ) إلى آخرِهِ : يشير إلى أنَّ الأعمال ليسَتْ علَّةً عقليةً لاستحقاق ثواب ولا عقاب ؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ وجوب استواء الأفعالِ كلّها بالنسبة إليهِ تعالى ، وما أُثيبَ عليه منها أو عُوقب فهو بمحض فضلِهِ تعالى أو عدلِهِ ، وإِنَّما الأفعال علامات مخلوقة الله تعالى ، بيَّنَ الشرعُ ما اختار الله سبحانَهُ أَنْ تدلَّ عليهِ مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يكونَ بينَهما ربط عقلي ، وتسمية الثواب والعقاب جزاءً ؛ لأنَّهما في صورة الجزاء ؛ لسبق ما يدل عليه شرعاً وقد وردَ : أَنَّهُ سبحانه يخلقُ لفضلة النارِ قوماً يُعذِّبُهم ولفضلةِ الجنَّةِ قوماً يُنعمُهم بها مِنْ غيرِ أن يسبق عمل للفريقين فقد روى البخاري ( ٧٤٤٩ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً في اختصام الجنة والنار إلى ربهما ، وفيه : « فقال الله تعالى للجنَّةِ : أنتِ رحمتي ، وقال للنارِ : أنتِ عذابي ، أُصيب بكِ مَنْ أَشَاءُ ، ولكلّ واحدةٍ منكما ملؤُها ، قال : فأمَّا الجنَّةُ فإِنَّ اللهَ لا يظلمُ مِنْ خلقِهِ أحداً ، وإِنَّهُ ينشئ للنارِ مَنْ يشاءُ ، فيُلقَونَ فيها ... » الحديث ، وعند البخاري ( ٦٦٦١ ) ، ومسلم ( ٢٨٤٦ ) ما يعارضه ؛ فإنما ينشئ خلقاً لفضلة الجنة لا النار ، وعليه : فالحديث مقلوب ، وهو - إن سُلَّمَ أنه ليس بمقلوب ـ لا ينافي عدل الله تعالى مالك الملك ، قال العلامة الكرماني في ( الكواكب الدراري ) ( ٢٥/ ١٦٠ ) : ( لا محذور في تعذيب الله تعالى من لا ذنب له ؛ إذ القاعدة القائلة بالحسن والقبح باطلة ، فلو عذَّبه لكان عدلاً ، والإنشاء للجنة لا ينافي الإنشاء للنار والله تعالى يفعل ما يشاء ، فلا حاجة إلى الحمل على الوهم ) . قال الحافظ في فتح الباري ( ١٣ / ٤٣٦ ) : ( قال أبو الحسن القابسي : المعروف في هذا الموضع أن الله ينشئ للجنة خلقاً ، وأما النار فيضع فيها قدمه ، قال : ولا أعلم في شيء من الأحاديث أنه ينشئ للنار خلقاً إلا هذا ) ، أو يحمل إنشاء خلْقٍ للنار بزيادة جسم الكافر حتى إن ضرسه كجبل أحد كما ورد ، كما ذكره بعض المحققين ، وهو جمع حسن . وكلا النوعين دال على سَعَةِ مُلكِهِ ، وانقيادِ جميع الممكنات لإرادته، وعدم تعاصيها على باهر قدرته كل منها واقع على ما ينبغي مِنْ جريهِ على وَفْقِ علمِهِ وإرادتِهِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يتجدَّدَ له بذلك كمال أو نقص حالاً ولا مآلاً ؛ فالوجوبُ إذا والظلمُ عليهِ محالانِ ؛ إذ الوجوب يستدعي تعاصي بعض الممكناتِ والظلم يستدعي التصرُّفَ على خلاف ما ينبغي.
His statement: "So He glorified, may He be exalted, whoever He willed" to its end: It indicates that actions are not rational causes for deserving reward or punishment; because you have known the necessity of all actions being equal with respect to Him, Exalted. What is rewarded or punished among them is purely by His grace or justice. Rather, actions are created signs of Allah, Exalted. The Law has clarified what Allah, glorified be He, chose that they should indicate, without there being any rational connection between them. The naming of reward and punishment as recompense is because they are in the form of recompense, due to the prior indication by Law. And it has been reported that He, glorified, creates people for the surplus of the Fire to punish them, and for the surplus of Paradise to bless them, without any preceding deed from either group. Al-Bukhari narrated (7449) from the hadith of Abu Huraira, may Allah be pleased with him, raised to the Prophet, concerning the dispute of Paradise and Hell before their Lord, including: "Allah, Exalted, said to Paradise: 'You are My mercy,' and to Hell: 'You are My punishment; I afflict whomever I will with you, and each of you will have its fill.' He said: 'As for Paradise, indeed Allah does not wrong anyone from His creation, and indeed He creates for the Fire whomever He wills, and they will be thrown into it...'" the hadith. And according to al-Bukhari (6661) and Muslim (2846) there is what contradicts it: that He only creates created beings for the surplus of Paradise, not the Fire. Therefore, the hadith is inverted. And even if it is granted that it is not inverted, it does not contradict the justice of Allah, the Owner of the Kingdom. Al-`Allama al-Kirmani said in al-Kawakib al-Darari (25/160): "There is no harm in Allah's punishing one who has no sin, for the principle of good and evil [by reason] is false. So if He punished him, it would be justice. And creating for Paradise does not negate creating for the Fire. Allah does what He wills, so there is no need to interpret it as a mistake." Al-Hafiz said in Fath al-Bari (13/436): "Abu al-Hasan al-Qabisi said: The known [version] in this place is that Allah creates created beings for Paradise, and as for the Fire, He places His foot in it. He said: I do not know in any hadith that He creates for the Fire created beings except this one." Or it is interpreted as creating creation for the Fire by increasing the body of the disbeliever until his molar is like Mount Uhud, as mentioned by some investigators, and that is a good reconciliation. And both types indicate the vastness of His dominion, and the submission of all possible things to His will, and their not resisting His overwhelming power. Each of them occurs as it ought, running in accordance with His knowledge and will, without there arising for Him thereby any perfection or deficiency, in the present state or ultimate outcome. Therefore, obligation and injustice are impossible with respect to Him; for obligation would require some possible things to resist, and injustice would require acting contrary to what is appropriate.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation and proof. It begins by commenting on a phrase from the matn: "فأكرم سبحانه من شاء" (So He honored whomever He willed). The commentator states that this indicates that actions are not rational causes (علة عقلية) for deserving reward or punishment. Why? Because all actions are equal in relation to God; none inherently deserves reward or punishment. Any reward or punishment is purely by God's grace or justice. Rather, actions are "created signs" (علامات مخلوقة) that God has designated through revelation to indicate what He wills. There is no rational link (ربط عقلي) between an act and its consequence; only divine decree makes the connection. The terms "recompense" (جزاء) are used metaphorically because they appear in the form of reward or punishment following a prior revealed indication.

Then he cites a hadith (reported by al-Bukhari) that God creates people for the surplus of Hell and Paradise without prior deeds. This is used to show that actions are not causes. He then addresses a textual difficulty: another version of the hadith suggests that only the creation for Paradise exists. Scholars reconcile this by noting that the hadith may be inverted, or that the creation for Hell refers to the enlargement of bodies of disbelievers. He quotes opinions of al-Kirmani and al-Hafiz. The conclusion: both possibilities (creating for Paradise and creating for Hell) demonstrate God's absolute dominion and the submission of all things to His will, without any change in God's perfection. Therefore, obligation (وجوب) and injustice (ظلم) are impossible regarding God, because obligation would imply resistance from some creatures, and injustice would imply acting contrary to what is appropriate, which is meaningless for God.

Key Terms
علة عقلية
علامات مخلوقة
ربط عقلي
جزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ash'aris deny any connection between actions and consequences altogether.
Correction: Ash'aris affirm a connection, but it is by divine decree and revelation, not by rational necessity. Actions are signs that Allah has linked to outcomes through His will.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why are actions not rational causes for reward or punishment?
A) Because actions are evil by nature
B) Because all actions are equal in relation to Allah, and reward/punishment is by His grace or justice
C) Because actions have no connection to reward or punishment
D) Because humans do not commit actions

Key Takeaway
Actions are signs created by Allah that indicate reward or punishment only by divine decree and revelation, not by any rational necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you feel a sense of entitlement to Allah's reward? How does it change your heart to know that your action is only a sign and that reward depends solely on His grace?
?
Consider a sin you struggle with. Do you fear punishment as if it is a necessary consequence, or do you see it as a sign that calls you to repentance, knowing that Allah's justice is not bound by your action?
?
If all actions are equal in Allah's sight, why do you sometimes pride yourself on your worship? What would it take for you to rely entirely on His mercy and not on your deeds?

The Hadith on Creating People for Hell and Paradise
Sanusi presents a hadith and discusses its textual variant and reconciliations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic hadith cited to prove that reward and punishment can occur without preceding deeds, and the scholarly reconciliation of its variant readings.

Core Idea
Reward and punishment can occur without any preceding act, showing they are not caused by actions.

Sanusi supports the claim that actions are not rational causes by citing a hadith in which Allah creates people directly for Hell and Paradise without any prior deeds. However, there is a textual variant that seems to contradict this. This lesson examines the hadith, the variant, and how scholars have reconciled them, reinforcing the Ash'ari position on the absolute sovereignty of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith report
Read the Arabic hadith text carefully. Notice that it says Allah creates people for the 'surplus of the Fire' and 'surplus of Paradise' without any preceding action.
This directly illustrates the point that deeds are not causes.
2
Identify the textual problem
There is another version (Bukhari 6661, Muslim 2846) that says Allah only creates for Paradise, not for the Fire. This creates a contradiction.
Scholars debate which version is authentic.
3
Understand the scholarly reconciliations
Some say the hadith is inverted (wording flipped). Others say it means the bodies of disbelievers are enlarged for punishment. Both interpretations preserve the point that actions are not causes.
Al-Kirmani and al-Hafiz offer arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فأكرمَ سبحانَهُ مَنْ شاءَ. ) إلى آخرِهِ : يشير إلى أنَّ الأعمال ليسَتْ علَّةً عقليةً لاستحقاق ثواب ولا عقاب ؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ وجوب استواء الأفعالِ كلّها بالنسبة إليهِ تعالى ، وما أُثيبَ عليه منها أو عُوقب فهو بمحض فضلِهِ تعالى أو عدلِهِ ، وإِنَّما الأفعال علامات مخلوقة الله تعالى ، بيَّنَ الشرعُ ما اختار الله سبحانَهُ أَنْ تدلَّ عليهِ مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يكونَ بينَهما ربط عقلي ، وتسمية الثواب والعقاب جزاءً ؛ لأنَّهما في صورة الجزاء ؛ لسبق ما يدل عليه شرعاً وقد وردَ : أَنَّهُ سبحانه يخلقُ لفضلة النارِ قوماً يُعذِّبُهم ولفضلةِ الجنَّةِ قوماً يُنعمُهم بها مِنْ غيرِ أن يسبق عمل للفريقين فقد روى البخاري ( ٧٤٤٩ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً في اختصام الجنة والنار إلى ربهما ، وفيه : « فقال الله تعالى للجنَّةِ : أنتِ رحمتي ، وقال للنارِ : أنتِ عذابي ، أُصيب بكِ مَنْ أَشَاءُ ، ولكلّ واحدةٍ منكما ملؤُها ، قال : فأمَّا الجنَّةُ فإِنَّ اللهَ لا يظلمُ مِنْ خلقِهِ أحداً ، وإِنَّهُ ينشئ للنارِ مَنْ يشاءُ ، فيُلقَونَ فيها ... » الحديث ، وعند البخاري ( ٦٦٦١ ) ، ومسلم ( ٢٨٤٦ ) ما يعارضه ؛ فإنما ينشئ خلقاً لفضلة الجنة لا النار ، وعليه : فالحديث مقلوب ، وهو - إن سُلَّمَ أنه ليس بمقلوب ـ لا ينافي عدل الله تعالى مالك الملك ، قال العلامة الكرماني في ( الكواكب الدراري ) ( ٢٥/ ١٦٠ ) : ( لا محذور في تعذيب الله تعالى من لا ذنب له ؛ إذ القاعدة القائلة بالحسن والقبح باطلة ، فلو عذَّبه لكان عدلاً ، والإنشاء للجنة لا ينافي الإنشاء للنار والله تعالى يفعل ما يشاء ، فلا حاجة إلى الحمل على الوهم ) . قال الحافظ في فتح الباري ( ١٣ / ٤٣٦ ) : ( قال أبو الحسن القابسي : المعروف في هذا الموضع أن الله ينشئ للجنة خلقاً ، وأما النار فيضع فيها قدمه ، قال : ولا أعلم في شيء من الأحاديث أنه ينشئ للنار خلقاً إلا هذا ) ، أو يحمل إنشاء خلْقٍ للنار بزيادة جسم الكافر حتى إن ضرسه كجبل أحد كما ورد ، كما ذكره بعض المحققين ، وهو جمع حسن . وكلا النوعين دال على سَعَةِ مُلكِهِ ، وانقيادِ جميع الممكنات لإرادته، وعدم تعاصيها على باهر قدرته كل منها واقع على ما ينبغي مِنْ جريهِ على وَفْقِ علمِهِ وإرادتِهِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يتجدَّدَ له بذلك كمال أو نقص حالاً ولا مآلاً ؛ فالوجوبُ إذا والظلمُ عليهِ محالانِ ؛ إذ الوجوب يستدعي تعاصي بعض الممكناتِ والظلم يستدعي التصرُّفَ على خلاف ما ينبغي.
His statement: "So He glorified, may He be exalted, whoever He willed" to its end: It indicates that actions are not rational causes for deserving reward or punishment; because you have known the necessity of all actions being equal with respect to Him, Exalted. What is rewarded or punished among them is purely by His grace or justice. Rather, actions are created signs of Allah, Exalted. The Law has clarified what Allah, glorified be He, chose that they should indicate, without there being any rational connection between them. The naming of reward and punishment as recompense is because they are in the form of recompense, due to the prior indication by Law. And it has been reported that He, glorified, creates people for the surplus of the Fire to punish them, and for the surplus of Paradise to bless them, without any preceding deed from either group. Al-Bukhari narrated (7449) from the hadith of Abu Huraira, may Allah be pleased with him, raised to the Prophet, concerning the dispute of Paradise and Hell before their Lord, including: "Allah, Exalted, said to Paradise: 'You are My mercy,' and to Hell: 'You are My punishment; I afflict whomever I will with you, and each of you will have its fill.' He said: 'As for Paradise, indeed Allah does not wrong anyone from His creation, and indeed He creates for the Fire whomever He wills, and they will be thrown into it...'" the hadith. And according to al-Bukhari (6661) and Muslim (2846) there is what contradicts it: that He only creates created beings for the surplus of Paradise, not the Fire. Therefore, the hadith is inverted. And even if it is granted that it is not inverted, it does not contradict the justice of Allah, the Owner of the Kingdom. Al-`Allama al-Kirmani said in al-Kawakib al-Darari (25/160): "There is no harm in Allah's punishing one who has no sin, for the principle of good and evil [by reason] is false. So if He punished him, it would be justice. And creating for Paradise does not negate creating for the Fire. Allah does what He wills, so there is no need to interpret it as a mistake." Al-Hafiz said in Fath al-Bari (13/436): "Abu al-Hasan al-Qabisi said: The known [version] in this place is that Allah creates created beings for Paradise, and as for the Fire, He places His foot in it. He said: I do not know in any hadith that He creates for the Fire created beings except this one." Or it is interpreted as creating creation for the Fire by increasing the body of the disbeliever until his molar is like Mount Uhud, as mentioned by some investigators, and that is a good reconciliation. And both types indicate the vastness of His dominion, and the submission of all possible things to His will, and their not resisting His overwhelming power. Each of them occurs as it ought, running in accordance with His knowledge and will, without there arising for Him thereby any perfection or deficiency, in the present state or ultimate outcome. Therefore, obligation and injustice are impossible with respect to Him; for obligation would require some possible things to resist, and injustice would require acting contrary to what is appropriate.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation and proof. It begins by commenting on a phrase from the matn: "فأكرم سبحانه من شاء" (So He honored whomever He willed). The commentator states that this indicates that actions are not rational causes (علة عقلية) for deserving reward or punishment. Why? Because all actions are equal in relation to God; none inherently deserves reward or punishment. Any reward or punishment is purely by God's grace or justice. Rather, actions are "created signs" (علامات مخلوقة) that God has designated through revelation to indicate what He wills. There is no rational link (ربط عقلي) between an act and its consequence; only divine decree makes the connection. The terms "recompense" (جزاء) are used metaphorically because they appear in the form of reward or punishment following a prior revealed indication.

Then he cites a hadith (reported by al-Bukhari) that God creates people for the surplus of Hell and Paradise without prior deeds. This is used to show that actions are not causes. He then addresses a textual difficulty: another version of the hadith suggests that only the creation for Paradise exists. Scholars reconcile this by noting that the hadith may be inverted, or that the creation for Hell refers to the enlargement of bodies of disbelievers. He quotes opinions of al-Kirmani and al-Hafiz. The conclusion: both possibilities (creating for Paradise and creating for Hell) demonstrate God's absolute dominion and the submission of all things to His will, without any change in God's perfection. Therefore, obligation (وجوب) and injustice (ظلم) are impossible regarding God, because obligation would imply resistance from some creatures, and injustice would imply acting contrary to what is appropriate, which is meaningless for God.

Key Terms
فضلة النار
فضلة الجنة
الوجوب
الظلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the variant hadith proves that Allah only creates for Paradise, contradicting the idea of reward/punishment without deeds.
Correction: Scholars reconcile by noting textual inversion or interpreting 'creation for Fire' as enlargement of bodies. Both versions ultimately affirm Allah's absolute sovereignty and that actions are not causes.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited by Sanusi (Bukhari 7449), what does Allah create for the surplus of the Fire?
A) Angels
B) People to punish them
C) Animals
D) Jinn

Key Takeaway
The hadith and its variant both support the doctrine that reward and punishment are not caused by actions but by Allah's will; any textual issues are resolvable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your good deeds are not the cause of your entry into Paradise, what is the true basis of your hope? Does that realization make you rely more on Allah's mercy or less?
?
The possibility that Allah could punish someone without any sin is affirmed in this lesson. How does that truth affect your fear of Allah and your sense of security in your own obedience? Are you willing to trust His justice even when it surpasses your understanding?
?
When you perform an act of worship, do you internally feel that Allah 'owes' you a reward? How does this lesson's teaching that actions are not causes challenge that feeling, and what must you change in your heart to make your worship purely for Him?

Divine Attributes
intermediate

Conclusion: Divine Dominion Excludes Obligation and Injustice
Sanusi concludes by affirming Allah's absolute dominion and the impossibility of obligation and injustice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why obligation and injustice are impossible for Allah, based on His absolute dominion and the submission of all creation to His will.

Core Idea
Allah's absolute sovereignty makes obligation and injustice unthinkable for Him.

In the final part of this passage, Sanusi draws the theological conclusion from the hadith discussion. Both interpretations of the hadith demonstrate Allah's vast dominion and the total submission of all possible things to His will. This leads to the axiom that obligation (وجوب) and injustice (ظلم) are impossible with respect to Allah, because they would imply resistance or acting contrary to what is appropriate—both impossible for the Sovereign.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding paragraph
Read from 'وكلا النوعين' to the end. Notice the emphasis on the vastness of Allah's dominion and the submission of all things.
The language is very emphatic about power and control.
2
Identify the two types of hadith interpretation
The passage mentions both interpretations (creation for Paradise and creation for Fire) and says both indicate the same thing: vast dominion and submission.
3
Understand what they indicate
They show that all possible things are subject to Allah's will and do not resist His power. Everything occurs as it ought according to His knowledge and will.
This reinforces Allah's complete control.
4
Grasp the impossibility of obligation and injustice
Obligation would require that some creatures can resist Allah's will, which is impossible. Injustice would mean acting contrary to what is appropriate, which is meaningless for the Absolute Sovereign.
This is a logical conclusion from the nature of divine power.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah can be unjust or that He is obligated to reward the obedient.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is obligation impossible with respect to Allah?
A) Because obligation would require Allah to do something He does not want

C) Because Allah is too perfect to be obligated
D) Because obligation is a human concept

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever harbored resentment against Allah because of a trial you faced, feeling that it was 'unjust'? How does this lesson's assertion that injustice is impossible for Allah challenge you to rethink your response to hardship? What would it mean for you to truly accept that everything that happens to you is exactly as it ought to be?
?
This lesson teaches that you cannot claim any right over Allah; obligation is impossible for Him. Does that make you feel unsettled, or does it free you from a ledger-like relationship with your Creator? How does this reshape the way you plead for His mercy or forgiveness?
?
If Allah's actions never add to or subtract from His perfection, then your obedience or sin does not affect Him. Yet you are still commanded to obey. In light of this, what is the only genuine motive left for your worship? How does this strip away any pretense of doing things for your own benefit and leave you with pure servitude?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
Reward and Punishment Do Not Affect God's Perfection
Sanusi explains that reward and punishment do not change God's perfection, making obligation and injustice impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that reward and punishment are manifestations of God's sovereignty and occur according to His will without adding to or detracting from His perfection, making obligation and injustice impossible for Him.

Core Idea
God's perfection is unchanged by reward and punishment; they show His absolute power.

In this passage, Sanusi establishes that both reward and punishment are not random events but deliberate acts that align perfectly with God's knowledge and will. He emphasizes that they do not result in any change in God's attributes—He remains eternally perfect. This leads to the crucial conclusion that God cannot be obligated to do anything, nor can He ever commit injustice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation to get a sense of the argument. The passage is concise but dense.
Focus on the flow from the purpose of reward/punishment to the logical conclusion.
2
Identify the two things both types indicate
Sanusi says they indicate God's vast sovereignty and the submission of all contingent beings to His will. Also note that they occur exactly as they should.
3
Understand the conclusion about obligation and injustice
Because God acts according to His knowledge and will, and no perfection or deficiency arises, obligation (being forced) and injustice (acting wrongly) are impossible. Think about why obligation would require disobedience and injustice would require acting contrary to what is appropriate.

وكلا النوعين دال على سَعَةِ مُلكِهِ ، وانقيادِ جميع الممكنات لإرادته، وعدم تعاصيها على باهر قدرته كل منها واقع على ما ينبغي مِنْ جريهِ على وَفْقِ علمِهِ وإرادتِهِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يتجدَّدَ له بذلك كمال أو نقص حالاً ولا مآلاً ; فالوجوبُ إذا والظلمُ عليهِ محالانِ ; إذ الوجوب يستدعي تعاصي بعض الممكناتِ والظلم يستدعي التصرُّفَ على خلاف ما ينبغي . 6 رحمتي ، وقال للنارِ : أنتِ عذابي ، أُصيب بكِ مَنْ أَشَاءُ ، ولكلّ واحدةٍ منكما ملؤُها ، قال : فأمَّا الجنَّةُ فإِنَّ اللهَ لا يظلمُ مِنْ خلقِهِ أحداً ، وإِنَّهُ ينشى للنارِ مَنْ يشاءُ ، فيُلقَونَ فيها ... » الحديث ، وعند البخاري ( ٦٦٦١ ) ، ومسلم ( ٢٨٤٦ ) ما يعارضه ; فإنما ينشئ خلقاً لفضلة الجنة لا النار ، وعليه : فالحديث مقلوب ، وهو - إن سُلَّمَ أنه ليس بمقلوب ـ لا ينافي عدل الله تعالى مالك الملك ، قال العلامة الكرماني في ( الكواكب الدراري » ( ٢٥/ ١٦٠ ) : ( لا محذور في تعذيب الله تعالى من لا ذنب له ; إذ القاعدة القائلة بالحسن والقبح باطلة ، فلو عذَّبه لكان عدلاً ، والإنشاء للجنة لا ينافي الإنشاء للنار والله تعالى يفعل ما يشاء ، فلا حاجة إلى الحمل على الوهم ) . قال الحافظ في فتح الباري ) ( ١٣ / ٤٣٦ ) : ( قال أبو الحسن القابسي : المعروف في هذا الموضع أن الله ينشئ للجنة خلقاً ، وأما النار فيضع فيها قدمه ، قال : ولا أعلم في شيء من الأحاديث أنه ينشئ للنار خلقاً إلا هذا ) ، أو يحمل إنشاء خلْقٍ للنار بزيادة جسم الكافر حتى إن ضرسه كجبل أحد كما ورد ، كما ذكره بعض المحققين ، وهو جمع حسن . مراده بكلا النوعين : الثواب والعقاب ; أي : إذا نظرت إلى الثواب وما احتوَتْ عليهِ الجنَّةُ مِنْ دقائقِ النعيم الخارقة للعوائد التي لم تخطر قط على بال ، وإلى مثلِها مِنْ دقائقِ العذابِ وما احتوَتْ عليهِ جهَنَّمُ مِنْ أنواع العذابِ التي لا تُكيَّفُ .. كلُّ ذلكَ لا يُوجِبُ له سبحانَهُ تجدُّدَ كمال لذاتِهِ ولا لصفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ ; حتى يجب ذلك عليه ، بل كلُّ كمال يليقُ بهِ فلم يزل متّصفاً بهِ في الأزلِ ولا يزال (۱) ، ولا يُوجِبُ لهُ فعله أو تركه نقصاً حتى يستحيل عليه . وأما فائدتها بالنسبة إلينا : فهي مستويةٌ في دلالتها على وجودِهِ تعالى ووجود صفاته العليَّةِ وسَعَةِ جلالِهِ وعظيم جماله ، بل لم يزدنا وقوع النوعين وخلْقُهُ تعالى الأضداد إلا قوَّةَ علم بعظيم اختيارِهِ وسَعَةِ مُلْكِهِ ، وأنَّهُ ليسَ مجبوراً على فعل من الأفعال
And both types indicate the vastness of His sovereignty, and the submission of all contingent beings to His will, and their non-disobedience to His overwhelming power. Each of them occurs as it should, in accordance with His knowledge and will, without any perfection or deficiency becoming renewed for Him by that, neither in state nor in outcome. So obligation upon Him and injustice from Him are impossible; for obligation would require the disobedience of some contingent beings, and injustice would require acting contrary to what is appropriate. 'My mercy... and He said to the Fire: You are My punishment, I afflict with you whom I will, and each of you has its fill.' He said: 'As for Paradise, God does not wrong any of His creation, and He creates for the Fire whom He wills, and they are cast into it...' the hadith. And with al-Bukhari (6661) and Muslim (2846) is what contradicts it; for He only creates people for the surplus of Paradise, not the Fire. Therefore the hadith is inverted. And if it is conceded that it is not inverted, it does not contradict the justice of God, the Owner of dominion. The scholar al-Kirmani said in 'al-Kawakib al-Darari' (25/160): 'There is no harm in God tormenting someone who has no sin, for the principle of good and evil is false; if He tormented him, it would be just. And creating for Paradise does not negate creating for the Fire; God does what He wills, so there is no need to interpret it as an illusion.' Al-Hafiz said in 'Fath al-Bari' (13/436): 'Abu al-Hasan al-Qabisi said: The well-known in this place is that God creates people for Paradise; as for the Fire, He places His foot in it. He said: I do not know of any hadith that says He creates people for the Fire except this one.' Or it is interpreted as creating people for the Fire by increasing the body of the disbeliever until his molar is like Mount Uhud, as mentioned, as some investigators mentioned, and this is a good reconciliation. His intention by 'both types' is reward and punishment; meaning: if you look at reward and what Paradise contains of subtle blessings that break customs which have never crossed the mind, and at similar subtle torments and what Hell contains of types of torment that cannot be described... all of that does not necessitate for Him, exalted, a renewal of perfection in His essence or in any of His attributes, such that it would be obligatory upon Him. Rather, every perfection befitting Him never ceases to be attributed to Him in pre-eternity and will never cease (1), nor does His doing or leaving it necessitate any deficiency that would be impossible for Him. And as for their benefit with respect to us: they are equal in their indication of His existence, exalted, and the existence of His sublime attributes, the vastness of His majesty, and the greatness of His beauty. Rather, the occurrence of the two types and His creation, exalted, of opposites only increased us in strength of knowledge of His tremendous choice and the vastness of His sovereignty, and that He is not compelled to any act.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part theological argument. First, Sanusi states that both reward and punishment (the 'two types') demonstrate God's vast sovereignty and the submission of all contingent things to His will. They occur exactly as He knows and wills, without any new perfection or deficiency accruing to God. This leads to the conclusion that obligation (being forced) and injustice (acting wrongly) are impossible for God. He then addresses a hadith that might appear to contradict this: the hadith about God creating people for Paradise and the Fire. After citing it and its apparent conflict with other hadith, Sanusi reports scholarly responses—that the hadith may be inverted or that it does not conflict with God's justice because the principle of good and evil (al-husn wa al-qubh) is false. He also mentions interpretations that the creation for the Fire refers to enlarging the bodies of disbelievers. Then Sanusi clarifies that by 'both types' he means reward and punishment. He explains that the extremes of blessings and torments do not cause any change in God's perfection; He is eternally perfect. Finally, he states that the benefit of these types for us is that they equally indicate God's existence, attributes, majesty, and beauty, and increase our knowledge of His absolute choice and sovereignty.

Key Terms
ثواب
عقاب
كمال
نقص
وجوب
ظلم
ممكنات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's action of rewarding and punishing adds to His perfection or is necessary for His justice.
Correction: God's actions do not change His perfection; He is perfectly the same before and after. Obligation and injustice are impossible for Him.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why are obligation and injustice impossible for God?
A) Because God is merciful and would never be unjust.
B) Because God's actions are always in accordance with His knowledge and will and do not change His perfection.
C) Because reward and punishment are illusions.
D) Because God is compelled to reward goodness.

Key Takeaway
Reward and punishment demonstrate God's absolute will and power without affecting His eternal perfection, making obligation and injustice impossible for Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every trial and blessing you receive is from God's perfect will, leaving no room for you to accuse Him of injustice? Examine your heart: when you suffer, do you ever question God's fairness? Commit to surrendering to His decree, knowing that He never acts inappropriately.
?
If you think your good deeds 'deserve' reward, are you unknowingly implying an obligation upon God? How does this lesson free you from expecting reward as a right? Resolve to worship God out of love and servitude, not entitlement.
?
Seeing reward and punishment in this world, do you view them as signs of God's absolute sovereignty or as changes in His nature? Let this truth transform your awe of God: He is perfect and unaffected by His creation. Ponder this until your heart trembles with reverence.

Reconciling a Hadith on Creation for Paradise and Fire with God's Justice, and the Benefit of Reward and Punishment
Sanusi discusses a hadith on creation for Paradise and Fire and explains the benefit of reward and punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars reconcile a hadith that might seem to imply God creates people specifically for punishment, and that the true benefit of reward and punishment is to increase our knowledge of God's sovereignty.

Core Idea
God's justice is not limited by human standards; reward and punishment teach us about His absolute power and choice.

In this portion, Sanusi addresses a hadith that might appear to contradict God's perfection by saying He creates people for the Fire. He presents scholarly responses that reconcile this with divine justice. He then clarifies that the ultimate benefit of reward and punishment is to demonstrate God's existence, attributes, and sovereignty, deepening our understanding of His absolute choice.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the initial scholarly responses
Notice the apparent conflict: two versions of a hadith. Scholars suggest it may be inverted or interpreted differently.
The hadith is from a specific source; note that Sanusi is not affirming it as sound but discussing it.
2
Understand the principle of 'al-husn wa al-qubh' being false
Al-Kirmani argues that God can do as He wills without being bound by human notions of justice; creating people for the Fire is not unjust.
This is a key theological point in Ash'ari theology.
3
Recognize the benefit for us
Sanusi concludes that reward and punishment equally indicate God's existence, attributes, and sovereignty, and increase our knowledge of His free choice and power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means God creates people for the sole purpose of tormenting them, which would be unjust.
Correction: Scholars interpret the hadith differently; either it is inverted, or creation for the Fire refers to enlargement of bodies, or God's justice allows it because the principle of good and evil is false.

Checkpoint
According to al-Kirmani's argument, why does creating people for the Fire not contradict God's justice?
A) Because God only creates for Paradise.
B) Because the hadith is not authentic.
C) Because the principle of good and evil (al-husn wa al-qubh) is false, so God can do as He wills.
D) Because the Fire is not real.

Key Takeaway
Scholars reconcile the hadith on creation for the Fire with God's justice by various interpretations, and the ultimate benefit of reward and punishment is to know God's absolute sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted God's justice when faced with suffering or apparent unfairness? How does this lesson challenge your entitlement to a certain outcome?
?
Are you willing to submit to a God whose will is not bound by your sense of right and wrong? What would that look like in your daily decisions?
?
If reward and punishment ultimately point to God's sovereignty rather than your merit, what truly motivates your obedience? Is it love of reward or fear of punishment, or something deeper?
