Why God Cannot Act for a Purpose
Sanusi proves that God cannot act for a purpose using two rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic theologians hold that God cannot act for a purpose (gharad), and how Sanusi proves this using two rational arguments.

Core Idea
God's actions are not for any purpose—purpose implies need, and God is free of need.

One of the key principles of Islamic theology is that Allah is absolutely free and self-sufficient. In this passage, Sanusi argues that if God acted for a purpose, that purpose would either compel Him or fail to be a true cause. Either way, it would compromise His transcendence. We will now examine Sanusi's concise proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the core argument.
Notice how Sanusi uses a conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
2
Analyse the first argument
Identify why a purpose would necessitate action. Consider the logic: if the purpose is a cause, it obligates; otherwise it is not a cause at all.
The verse is cited to reinforce God's absolute freedom.
3
Analyse the second argument
Consider the purpose's origin: if pre-eternal, the act must also be pre-eternal, which is false for created acts.
Sanusi references an earlier proof (برهان) which we assume establishes that originated acts are not eternal.
4
Connect to divine attributes
See how both arguments uphold God's sovereignty (qudra) and self-sufficiency (ghina).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومِنْ هنا استحالَ أنْ يكونَ فعلهُ تعالى لغرض ; لأنَّهُ لو كانَ لهُ غرض في الفعل لأوجبَهُ عليه ، وإلا لم يكن علة له ، فيكونُ مقهوراً ، كيف ﴿ وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَخْتَارُ ﴾ وأيضاً : فالغرضُ إِمَّا قديم فيلزم قدم الفعل ، وقد مرَّ برهان (۱)
And from here it becomes impossible that His act, exalted, be for a purpose; because if He had a purpose in the act, it would necessitate it upon Him, otherwise it would not be a cause for it, and He would be compelled. How? 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses.' And also: the purpose is either pre-eternal, then the pre-eternality of the act follows, and the proof has already passed (1).
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a concise proof (burhan) that God cannot act for a purpose (gharad). Sanusi argues: if God had a purpose in His action, that purpose would either obligate Him to act or not. If it obligates Him, then He is compelled (maqhuran), which contradicts His absolute sovereignty. If it does not obligate Him, then it is not a true cause ('illah) for the act. The phrase 'How? 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses'' cites the Qur'an to emphasize God's unrestricted freedom. Then Sanusi adds a second argument: the purpose is either pre-eternal (qadim) or originated. If it is pre-eternal, then the act would also have to be pre-eternal, which is false for originated acts. The proof for that point has been given earlier (and is presumably on a later page). Thus both alternatives lead to impossibility.

Key Terms
غرض
علة
مقهور
قدم الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God acts for a purpose, just as humans act to achieve goals.
Correction: Kalam shows that a purpose implies a need or deficiency in the agent, which is impossible for God. His actions are free and self-sufficient.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what would follow if God had a purpose in His actions?
A) He would be more perfect.
B) He would be compelled or the purpose would not be a true cause.
C) His actions would be unjust.
D) He would gain new knowledge.

Key Takeaway
God's actions are free from any external purpose; they flow from His will and wisdom without being motivated by need or deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever secretly believed that God owes you something—like a reward for your good deeds—and thus you treat your relationship with Him as transactional? Does that hidden assumption reveal that you attribute purpose or need to God? Commit to recognizing today that every blessing from God is purely a gift, not a payment.
?
When you pray or perform acts of worship, do you sometimes feel that God needs your worship or that your actions 'complete' something in His plan? This lesson declares that God is absolutely free of any purpose or need. If you truly internalize that, how would your worship change from being a request-driven transaction to a pure expression of love and submission?
?
You often ask 'Why did God allow this hardship?' as if His actions must have a purpose that you can understand. But the lesson shows that God's actions have no external purpose—they flow from His will without need. Can you accept that some events in your life simply are without a purpose you can grasp, and that your trust in God must be independent of your need for explanations? Reflect on whether you can surrender the need to understand and instead submit to His absolute freedom.

God's Actions Cannot Be for a Purpose: Obligation and Infinite Regress
Sanusi presents two initial arguments against God acting for a purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's actions cannot be motivated by a purpose, focusing on the arguments that a purpose would obligate Him or lead to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
A purpose would make God subjugated; an eternal or temporal purpose both lead to contradiction.

Sanusi begins by establishing that God's absolute freedom precludes any external compulsion. He then presents two powerful arguments: first, that a purpose would obligate God and compromise His sovereignty; second, that any purpose, whether eternal or temporal, leads to an impossibility. Let's examine these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the Qur'anic verse citation marks the first argument.
2
Identify the first argument
The passage states that if God had a purpose, it would obligate Him, making Him subjugated (maqhūr). This contradicts the Qur'anic verse that asserts God's absolute freedom to create and choose.
3
Identify the second argument
The purpose is considered either eternal or temporal. If eternal, the action would be eternal, but actions are proven temporal. If temporal, it would require another purpose, leading to an infinite regress, which is invalid.
This is a classic kalam argument against infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومِنْ هنا استحالَ أنْ يكونَ فعلهُ تعالى لغرض ؛ لأنَّهُ لو كانَ لهُ غرض في الفعل لأوجبَهُ عليه ، وإلا لم يكن علة له ، فيكونُ مقهوراً ، كيف ﴿ وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَخْتَارُ ﴾ ؟!
وأيضاً : فالغرضُ إِمَّا قديم فيلزم قدم الفعل ، وقد مرَّ برهان حدوثِهِ ، أو حادث فيفتقر إلى غرض ، ثم كذلك ويتسلسل فيؤدي إلى حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها ، وقد مرَّ بطلانه (۱)
وأيضاً : فالغرضُ إِمَّا مصلحةٌ تعود إليه ، أو إلى فعله ،
والأوَّلُ محالٌ ؛ لاستلزام اتصاف ذاته العليَّةِ بالحوادث
!
والثاني محالٌ ؛ لعدم وجوبِ مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح ولأنَّه قادر على إيصال تلك المصلحة إلى العبد مثلاً بغير واسطة ، ولأنَّهُ يلزمُ فيهِ تعليلُ الشيء بنفسِهِ ، أو التسلسل لنقل الكلام إلى تلك المصلحة نفسها
يعني : أَنَّكَ إذا عرفت استواء الأفعالِ بالنسبة إليهِ تعالى ، وأنه مختار في جميعها لا يجب عليهِ منها شيء.. لزمَ ألا يكونَ لهُ تعالى غرض في شيء منها ؛ أي: لا علَّةَ لشيءٍ مِنَ الأفعالِ مشتملة على حكمة تبعثه على إيجادِ ذلك الفعل أو إعدامِهِ (۲) ، بل هو جلَّ وعلا مختار في كلا
And from this it is impossible that His, Most High, action be for a purpose; because if He had a purpose in the action, it would obligate it upon Him, otherwise it would not be a cause for it, and He would be subjugated. How (and your Lord creates what He wills and chooses)! (Q 28:68)
Also: the purpose is either eternal, so the eternity of the action would follow, and the proof of its temporality has already passed; or temporal, so it would need a purpose, and so on, leading to an infinite regress of temporal events without a first, and its invalidity has already passed (1).
Also: the purpose is either a benefit returning to Him or to His action.
The first is impossible because it necessitates attributing temporal events to His exalted essence!
The second is impossible because of the absence of obligation to observe what is good and what is most good, and because He is able to convey that benefit to the servant, for example, without an intermediary, and because it would imply either explaining a thing by itself or infinite regress when transferring the discussion to that same benefit.
Meaning: when you know the equality of actions relative to Him, Most High, and that He is free in all of them, nothing being obligatory upon Him from them... then it follows that He, Most High, has no purpose in any of them; that is, no cause for any action containing a wisdom that would impel Him to bring that action into existence or to annihilate it (2). Rather, He, Glorious and Most High, is free in both
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage refutes the idea that God acts for a purpose (gharaḍ). The author provides multiple proofs. First, if God had a purpose, that purpose would obligate Him to act, making Him subjugated (maqhūr)—contradicting His absolute freedom (Qur'an 28:68). Second, the purpose is either eternal or temporal. If eternal, the action would be eternal, but actions are proven temporal. If temporal, it would require another purpose, leading to infinite regress of temporal events, which is impossible. Third, the purpose is either a benefit to God or to His action. Benefit to God is impossible because it would attribute temporal events to His essence. Benefit to His action is impossible because: a) God is not obligated to observe what is best (al-aṣlaḥ); b) He can directly grant benefit without intermediary; c) it leads to either explaining a thing by itself or infinite regress. The conclusion: given that actions are equal relative to God and He is absolutely free, He has no purpose or cause impelling Him; He acts purely by choice.

Key Terms
غرض
علة
مقهور
قديم
حادث
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'purpose' simply means any reason or wisdom behind an action.
Correction: In this context, 'purpose' (gharaḍ) means an external compelling cause that obligates the agent, not merely wisdom (ḥikma) that does not necessitate action.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one consequence if God's purpose were temporal?
A) The action would be eternal.
B) It would lead to an infinite regress.
C) God would be subjugated.
D) The purpose would be unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
God's freedom precludes any external purpose that would obligate Him or lead to an infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself trying to justify God’s actions to yourself or others, as if He needs a reason that makes sense to you? Does that reveal a hidden assumption that God is accountable to your standards? What would it take today to let go of that need for justification and simply trust His freedom?
?
When life feels purposeless or unfair, do you instinctively demand to know the 'why' behind God's decree? How does this lesson challenge your insistence on understanding the purpose behind every trial? Are you willing to submit without needing to see the reason?
?
If God’s actions are not compelled by any purpose, does that make you uneasy, as if His actions might be arbitrary? Or does it deepen your trust, knowing that His freedom is absolute and not subject to external forces? Examine your heart: do you truly worship a God who answers to no one, not even to your own sense of justice?

God's Actions Cannot Be for a Purpose: The Argument from Benefit
Sanusi presents the third argument against purpose, focusing on the impossibility of benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's actions cannot aim at any benefit, whether for Himself or for His creation.

Core Idea
Any benefit from God's action is either impossible or unnecessary, and would lead to absurdity.

Sanusi continues his proof by examining the possibility that God acts for a benefit (maṣlaḥa). He divides benefits into two categories: those returning to God and those returning to His action. He shows both are impossible, thereby reinforcing God's absolute freedom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the division of benefits and the multiple reasons given.
The passage ends mid-sentence due to a page break.
2
Identify the two categories of benefit
The passage divides the purpose (gharaḍ) into benefit (maṣlaḥa) returning to God or to His action. Understand each category.
3
Understand why benefit to God is impossible
Benefit to God is impossible because it would necessitate attributing temporal events (ḥawādith) to His essence, which is incompatible with His perfection.
4
Understand why benefit to His action is impossible
Three reasons are given: (1) God is not obligated to observe what is best (al-aṣlaḥ); (2) He can directly convey benefit without an intermediary action; (3) it would lead to explaining a thing by itself or infinite regress.
These reasons reinforce that no benefit can be a purpose for God's actions.
5
Reflect on the concluding meaning
The final 'meaning' paragraph clarifies that having no purpose does not mean actions are without wisdom; rather, it means no compelling cause. God acts purely by choice.
This resolves a common misunderstanding.

?

?

How does the absolute freedom of God in this passage shatter that assumption? What would change if you truly internalized that God owes you nothing, yet still acts?

The First Proof: Purpose Would Compel God
Sanusi presents the first proof against purposes in God's acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing a purpose to God's action would make the act obligatory and thus contradict His free choice.

Core Idea
If God had a purpose, He would be compelled, not free.

The first proof Sanusi presents argues directly from the definition of purpose. To have a purpose means the act contains a wisdom that rationally impels the agent to do it, such that not doing it would be a deficiency. Scripture confirms God's absolute freedom of choice, so no act of His can be motivated by a purpose that would obligate Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Follow Sanusi's step-by-step reasoning: purpose definition, entailment of obligation, and the conclusion that God would be coerced.
Pay attention to the terms غرض and الملازمة.
2
Identify the two parts of the proof
The passage first explains the entailment (ملازمة) between purpose and obligation, then argues that obligation contradicts God's free choice.
The second part is introduced by 'فيكون مقهوراً'.
3
Reflect on the scriptural support
The verse from Al-Qasas is used to confirm that God chooses freely.
The verse emphasizes both creation and choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدل في العقيدة على هذا المطلب بأوجه : الأول : أنَّهُ لو كانَ لهُ غرضُ في فعلِ مِنَ الأفعالِ لكانَ ذلكَ الفعَلُ واجباً عليه ، لا يتأتّى له تركُهُ ، وبيانُ الملازمة : أنَّ معنى الغرضِ : أن يشتمل الفعل على حكمة تبعثه عقلاً على إيجادِهِ ؛ بحيثُ يلزم نقصُهُ لو لم يفعل ، هذا معنى الغرض ، فيكون موجباً للفعل ، وإلا لم يكن غرضاً له علة فيهِ فقولي : ( وإلا لم يكن علَّةٌ لهُ ( بيان للملازمة ، وأما قولي : ( فيكونُ مقهوراً ) فهو بيان للثانية ؛ وهي قولنا : لكنَّه لا يكونُ الفعلُ واجباً عليه ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ قهرِهِ وعدم اختياره ؛ إذ المختار هو الذي يتأتّى منه الفعلُ والتركُ ، والفَرْضُ أَنَّ هذا الفعلَ فيهِ غرضُ لا يتأتّى معَهُ تركُهُ ، وقد علمت فيما سبق وجوبَ كونه جل وعلا مختاراً ، فبطل إذا أنْ يكونَ في فعلٍ مِنْ أفعالِهِ غرضُ يحمله على ، قال تعالى : ﴿ وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختارُ ﴾ [القصص : ٦٨] . الثاني : أنَّ الغرضَ : إما أن يكون قديماً فيجب قدم الفعل ، وإلا كانَ البارى جلَّ وعلا ناقصاً ؛ لفواتِ غرضِهِ ، أو حادثاً فيحتاج هذا الغرضُ إلى غرض حادثٍ ؛ إذْ هو مِنْ جملة الأفعال الحادثة ، ويلزمُ التسلسل وحوادث لا أوَّلَ لها ، وقدمُ الفعلِ باطل ؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ برهان حدوثِ العالم ، والتسلسل - وهو إثباتُ حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها - باطل ، وقد سبق برهانه (۱) الثالثُ : الغرضُ : إِمَّا مصلحة في الفعل تعود إليه تعالى ، أو مصلحة تعود إلى خلقه والأوَّلُ باطل ؛ لأنَّهُ يُوجِبُ اتِّصاف ذاته بالحوادثِ ، وقد مرَّ بطلانه ، ويُوجِبُ أيضاً أن يكون ناقصاً في ذاتِهِ ، وإنما تكمل بأفعاله . والثاني باطل ؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ عدم وجوب مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح عليهِ تعالى ، ولأنَّ غرض العبد إنَّما هو حصول لذة له ، أو دفع ألم ، والله سبحانَهُ قادر على إيصال ذلك له بغيرِ واسطة فعلٍ . وأيضاً : ننقلُ الكلامَ إلى هذه المصلحة فنقول : ما الموجِبُ لخلقها ووجودها بواسطة الفعل ؟ فإن قيل : لذاتِ كونها مصلحة .. لزم تعليلُ الشيء بنفسِهِ ؛ لأنَّها صارَتْ غرض نفسها وإن قيلَ : لغرض زائدِ عليها .. نُقِلَ الكلامُ إلى ذلكَ الغرضِ ، ولزم التسلسل . 1 تعليلُ الفقهاء للأحكام بالجعل الشرعي ورعيه بالتفضل ] وكما عرفت وجوب نفي الغرض في أفعالِهِ تعالى كذلك يجب في أحكامه ، وما يذكرُهُ فقهاء أهل السنَّةِ مِنْ علل الأحكامِ إِنَّما هو بالجعْلِ
He argued in the doctrine for this claim with aspects: The first: That if He had a purpose in any of the acts, that act would be obligatory upon Him, not possible for Him to leave it. And the explanation of the entailment: That the meaning of purpose is that the act includes a wisdom that rationally impels Him to bring it about, such that His deficiency would be necessary if He did not do it. This is the meaning of purpose, so it would necessitate the act. Otherwise it would not be a purpose for which He is a cause. So my saying: (and otherwise it would not be a cause for Him) is an explanation of the entailment. And as for my saying: (so He would be coerced) it is an explanation of the second [part]; which is our saying: but the act is not obligatory upon Him, because of what follows from that of His coercion and lack of choice; for the chooser is the one from whom both act and abandonment are possible, and the assumption is that this act has a purpose with which its abandonment is not possible. And you have learned previously the necessity of His, may He be exalted, being a chooser. So it is nullified, therefore, that in any of His acts there be a purpose that impels Him to it. He said, exalted: {And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses} [Al-Qasas: 68]. The second: That the purpose: either it is eternal, then the act must be eternal, otherwise the Creator, may He be exalted, would be deficient due to the loss of His purpose; or it is originated, then this purpose needs an originated purpose, since it is among originated acts, and infinite regress and events without beginning would follow. And the eternity of the act is false, because of what you have known from the proof of the world's origination, and infinite regress — which is proving events without beginning — is false, and its proof has preceded (1). The third: The purpose: either a benefit in the act returning to Him, exalted, or a benefit returning to His creation. The first is false because it necessitates that His essence be characterized by originated things, and its falsehood has passed, and it also necessitates that He be deficient in His essence, only completing it through His acts. And the second is false because of what you have known of the non-obligation of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial upon Him, exalted, and because the purpose of the servant is only the attainment of pleasure for him, or the repulsion of pain, and God, glorified, is able to convey that to him without the intermediary of an act. And also: we transfer the discussion to this benefit and say: What necessitates its creation and existence through the act? If it is said: due to it being a benefit itself, then the thing would be caused by itself, because it became its own purpose. And if it is said: for an additional purpose beyond it, then the discussion is transferred to that purpose, and infinite regress would follow. 1 The jurists' explanation of rulings by legal stipulation and consideration by favor] And as you have known the necessity of negating purpose in His, exalted, acts, likewise it is necessary in His rulings. And what the jurists of the Ahl al-Sunnah mention of causes of rulings is only by stipulation.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage presents three proofs against the attribution of purposes (aghrad) to God's actions. The first proof argues that if God had a purpose, the act would be obligatory upon Him, contradicting His free choice. The second proof considers that if the purpose is eternal or originated, it leads to problems of temporal priority or infinite regress. The third proof divides purpose into benefit to God or to creation and shows both are false. The passage concludes by linking this to rulings: just as God's acts have no purpose, His rulings are not based on intrinsic causes but on divine stipulation.

Key Terms
الغرض
الملازمة
المختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying purpose means God acts arbitrarily or without wisdom.
Correction: Sanusi does not deny wisdom; he denies that wisdom compels God. God acts with wisdom but freely, not because He is obligated by it.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, if God had a purpose in an act, what would be the consequence?
A) The act would be optional.
B) The act would be obligatory and God would be coerced.
C) The act would be impossible.
D) God would become dependent on creation.

Key Takeaway
Purpose in God's acts would imply obligation and coercion, contradicting His absolute freedom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself expecting God to act according to your sense of what is 'wise' or 'fair', as if He owes you an explanation? How does Sanusi's argument that God has no compelling purpose challenge that expectation, and what should your response be when His acts are beyond your understanding?
?
If God were compelled by a purpose, He would not be free—yet many of us secretly wish God were predictable, controllable, a 'check-box' God who must reward good and punish evil on our terms. Which of your own hidden assumptions about God's actions need to be surrendered so you can truly worship a free Lord?
?
Sanusi says purpose would imply deficiency if omitted. When do you behave as if God's failure to act according to your plan means He is deficient? Repent of that presumption, and commit today to trusting His freedom over your expectations.

The Second Proof: The Dilemma of Purpose's Temporality
Sanusi presents the second proof based on the temporal nature of purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dilemma that if God's purpose is either eternal or originated, both lead to absurdities.

Core Idea
A purpose cannot be eternal or originated without leading to impossibility.

Sanusi's second proof examines the temporal status of the supposed purpose. If it is eternal, then the act must also be eternal, contradicting the world's origination. If it is originated, it would require another purpose, leading to infinite regress. Both options are false.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two options
The purpose must be either eternal (قديم) or originated (حادث). Consider each case.
These are the only logical possibilities.
2
Analyze the eternal case
If eternal, the act must be eternal to avoid God's deficiency, but the world is originated (برهان حدوث العالم).
3
Analyze the originated case
If originated, it needs another purpose, leading to infinite regress (تسلسل), which is impossible.
Infinite regress of purposes is logically invalid.
4
Conclude the impossibility
Since both options are false, the existence of a purpose is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدل في العقيدة على هذا المطلب بأوجه : الأول : أنَّهُ لو كانَ لهُ غرضُ في فعلِ مِنَ الأفعالِ لكانَ ذلكَ الفعَلُ واجباً عليه ، لا يتأتّى له تركُهُ ، وبيانُ الملازمة : أنَّ معنى الغرضِ : أن يشتمل الفعل على حكمة تبعثه عقلاً على إيجادِهِ ؛ بحيثُ يلزم نقصُهُ لو لم يفعل ، هذا معنى الغرض ، فيكون موجباً للفعل ، وإلا لم يكن غرضاً له علة فيهِ فقولي : ( وإلا لم يكن علَّةٌ لهُ ( بيان للملازمة ، وأما قولي : ( فيكونُ مقهوراً ) فهو بيان للثانية ؛ وهي قولنا : لكنَّه لا يكونُ الفعلُ واجباً عليه ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ قهرِهِ وعدم اختياره ؛ إذ المختار هو الذي يتأتّى منه الفعلُ والتركُ ، والفَرْضُ أَنَّ هذا الفعلَ فيهِ غرضُ لا يتأتّى معَهُ تركُهُ ، وقد علمت فيما سبق وجوبَ كونه جل وعلا مختاراً ، فبطل إذا أنْ يكونَ في فعلٍ مِنْ أفعالِهِ غرضُ يحمله على ، قال تعالى : ﴿ وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختارُ ﴾ [القصص : ٦٨] . الثاني : أنَّ الغرضَ : إما أن يكون قديماً فيجب قدم الفعل ، وإلا كانَ البارى جلَّ وعلا ناقصاً ؛ لفواتِ غرضِهِ ، أو حادثاً فيحتاج هذا الغرضُ إلى غرض حادثٍ ؛ إذْ هو مِنْ جملة الأفعال الحادثة ، ويلزمُ التسلسل وحوادث لا أوَّلَ لها ، وقدمُ الفعلِ باطل ؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ برهان حدوثِ العالم ، والتسلسل - وهو إثباتُ حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها - باطل ، وقد سبق برهانه (۱) الثالثُ : الغرضُ : إِمَّا مصلحة في الفعل تعود إليه تعالى ، أو مصلحة تعود إلى خلقه والأوَّلُ باطل ؛ لأنَّهُ يُوجِبُ اتِّصاف ذاته بالحوادثِ ، وقد مرَّ بطلانه ، ويُوجِبُ أيضاً أن يكون ناقصاً في ذاتِهِ ، وإنما تكمل بأفعاله . والثاني باطل ؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ عدم وجوب مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح عليهِ تعالى ، ولأنَّ غرض العبد إنَّما هو حصول لذة له ، أو دفع ألم ، والله سبحانَهُ قادر على إيصال ذلك له بغيرِ واسطة فعلٍ . وأيضاً : ننقلُ الكلامَ إلى هذه المصلحة فنقول : ما الموجِبُ لخلقها ووجودها بواسطة الفعل ؟ فإن قيل : لذاتِ كونها مصلحة .. لزم تعليلُ الشيء بنفسِهِ ؛ لأنَّها صارَتْ غرض نفسها وإن قيلَ : لغرض زائدِ عليها .. نُقِلَ الكلامُ إلى ذلكَ الغرضِ ، ولزم التسلسل . 1 تعليلُ الفقهاء للأحكام بالجعل الشرعي ورعيه بالتفضل ] وكما عرفت وجوب نفي الغرض في أفعالِهِ تعالى كذلك يجب في أحكامه ، وما يذكرُهُ فقهاء أهل السنَّةِ مِنْ علل الأحكامِ إِنَّما هو بالجعْلِ
He argued in the doctrine for this claim with aspects: The first: That if He had a purpose in any of the acts, that act would be obligatory upon Him, not possible for Him to leave it. And the explanation of the entailment: That the meaning of purpose is that the act includes a wisdom that rationally impels Him to bring it about, such that His deficiency would be necessary if He did not do it. This is the meaning of purpose, so it would necessitate the act. Otherwise it would not be a purpose for which He is a cause. So my saying: (and otherwise it would not be a cause for Him) is an explanation of the entailment. And as for my saying: (so He would be coerced) it is an explanation of the second [part]; which is our saying: but the act is not obligatory upon Him, because of what follows from that of His coercion and lack of choice; for the chooser is the one from whom both act and abandonment are possible, and the assumption is that this act has a purpose with which its abandonment is not possible. And you have learned previously the necessity of His, may He be exalted, being a chooser. So it is nullified, therefore, that in any of His acts there be a purpose that impels Him to it. He said, exalted: {And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses} [Al-Qasas: 68]. The second: That the purpose: either it is eternal, then the act must be eternal, otherwise the Creator, may He be exalted, would be deficient due to the loss of His purpose; or it is originated, then this purpose needs an originated purpose, since it is among originated acts, and infinite regress and events without beginning would follow. And the eternity of the act is false, because of what you have known from the proof of the world's origination, and infinite regress — which is proving events without beginning — is false, and its proof has preceded (1). The third: The purpose: either a benefit in the act returning to Him, exalted, or a benefit returning to His creation. The first is false because it necessitates that His essence be characterized by originated things, and its falsehood has passed, and it also necessitates that He be deficient in His essence, only completing it through His acts. And the second is false because of what you have known of the non-obligation of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial upon Him, exalted, and because the purpose of the servant is only the attainment of pleasure for him, or the repulsion of pain, and God, glorified, is able to convey that to him without the intermediary of an act. And also: we transfer the discussion to this benefit and say: What necessitates its creation and existence through the act? If it is said: due to it being a benefit itself, then the thing would be caused by itself, because it became its own purpose. And if it is said: for an additional purpose beyond it, then the discussion is transferred to that purpose, and infinite regress would follow. 1 The jurists' explanation of rulings by legal stipulation and consideration by favor] And as you have known the necessity of negating purpose in His, exalted, acts, likewise it is necessary in His rulings. And what the jurists of the Ahl al-Sunnah mention of causes of rulings is only by stipulation.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage presents three proofs against the attribution of purposes (aghrad) to God's actions. The first proof argues that if God had a purpose, the act would be obligatory upon Him, contradicting His free choice. The second proof considers that if the purpose is eternal or originated, it leads to problems of temporal priority or infinite regress. The third proof divides purpose into benefit to God or to creation and shows both are false. The passage concludes by linking this to rulings: just as God's acts have no purpose, His rulings are not based on intrinsic causes but on divine stipulation.

Key Terms
قديم
حادث
التسلسل
برهان حدوث العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the second proof say about a purpose that is originated?
A) It is possible if the act is also originated.
B) It leads to infinite regress.
C) It implies God is deficient.
D) It is the same as an eternal purpose.

Key Takeaway
Purpose cannot be eternal (contradicts world's origination) nor originated (leads to infinite regress).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make decisions, do you often seek a purpose that is separate from Allah? How does this proof challenge your reliance on independent purposes?
?
Are there areas in your life where you justify your actions by an endless chain of 'why'? How can you cut that chain by submitting to Allah's sovereignty, even when you don't see a purpose?
?
If Allah acts without purpose, how does that transform your understanding of your own trials—where you might search for a purpose that may not exist? Will you trust Him anyway?

Divine Attributes
intermediate

The Third Proof: No Benefit in God's Acts
Sanusi presents the third proof against purposes based on benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that purpose cannot be a benefit for God or for creation, and why.

Core Idea
Purpose cannot bring benefit to God (implying imperfection) or to creation (unnecessary).

The third proof considers that purpose, if it exists, must be either a benefit returning to God or to His creation. Sanusi shows both options false: benefit to God would mean His essence is subject to change and completion through actions, while benefit to creation is not obligatory upon God and can be achieved without acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of benefit
Purpose as benefit must either return to God (مصلحة تعود إليه) or to creation (مصلحة تعود لخلقه).
2
Refute benefit to God
Benefit for God implies God can receive benefits from actions, meaning His essence is temporal and needs completion, which is false.
This would attribute originated qualities to God.
3
Refute benefit to creation
Benefit for creation is not obligatory upon God, and God can provide benefit without acts. Also, seeking benefit implies desire or need, which is not His attribute.
Creatures seek benefit due to need, not God.
4
Additional argument: infinite regress
If the benefit itself requires a reason, it leads to either circularity or infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
Why is the option that purpose benefits God considered false?
A) God does not need benefits.
B) It would make God's essence changeable and incomplete without acts.
C) Benefits only apply to creation.

Key Takeaway
Purpose as benefit for God or creation is impossible; God is free from need and compulsion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that God owes you comfort or success because you are 'good'? How does Sanusi's argument that benefit is not obligatory upon God confront that belief?
?
When you face hardship, do you assume God is unjust or indifferent? How should the truth that God is perfect without any act change your reaction to difficulty?
?
Are you more focused on the benefit you get from your deeds (reward, pleasure) than on simple obedience? How might the argument against purpose based on benefit free you from self-interest in worship?

5 min
Negating Purposes in Divine Rulings
Sanusi extends the negation of purposes to divine rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the negation of purpose in God's acts extends to His rulings, and how jurists use 'causes' only as legal stipulations.

Core Idea
God's rulings, like His acts, have no intrinsic purposes; juristic causes are stipulations.

After establishing that God's acts have no purposes, Sanusi applies the same principle to His rulings. He clarifies that when scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah speak of 'causes' (علل) of rulings, they mean only that the rulings are attached to certain conditions by divine stipulation (جعل شرعي), not that God is motivated by some purpose.

Guided Path
1
Understand the extension from acts to rulings
The same necessity to negate purpose in acts applies to rulings.
2
Clarify the meaning of 'cause' in jurisprudence
Jurists' 'cause' (علة) is not a real efficient cause but a legal indicator by which the ruling is associated.
3
Appreciate the rational basis
This preserves God's absolute sovereignty and freedom in legislation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدل في العقيدة على هذا المطلب بأوجه : الأول : أنَّهُ لو كانَ لهُ غرضُ في فعلِ مِنَ الأفعالِ لكانَ ذلكَ الفعَلُ واجباً عليه ، لا يتأتّى له تركُهُ ، وبيانُ الملازمة : أنَّ معنى الغرضِ : أن يشتمل الفعل على حكمة تبعثه عقلاً على إيجادِهِ ؛ بحيثُ يلزم نقصُهُ لو لم يفعل ، هذا معنى الغرض ، فيكون موجباً للفعل ، وإلا لم يكن غرضاً له علة فيهِ فقولي : ( وإلا لم يكن علَّةٌ لهُ ( بيان للملازمة ، وأما قولي : ( فيكونُ مقهوراً ) فهو بيان للثانية ؛ وهي قولنا : لكنَّه لا يكونُ الفعلُ واجباً عليه ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ قهرِهِ وعدم اختياره ؛ إذ المختار هو الذي يتأتّى منه الفعلُ والتركُ ، والفَرْضُ أَنَّ هذا الفعلَ فيهِ غرضُ لا يتأتّى معَهُ تركُهُ ، وقد علمت فيما سبق وجوبَ كونه جل وعلا مختاراً ، فبطل إذا أنْ يكونَ في فعلٍ مِنْ أفعالِهِ غرضُ يحمله على ، قال تعالى : ﴿ وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختارُ ﴾ [القصص : ٦٨] . الثاني : أنَّ الغرضَ : إما أن يكون قديماً فيجب قدم الفعل ، وإلا كانَ البارى جلَّ وعلا ناقصاً ؛ لفواتِ غرضِهِ ، أو حادثاً فيحتاج هذا الغرضُ إلى غرض حادثٍ ؛ إذْ هو مِنْ جملة الأفعال الحادثة ، ويلزمُ التسلسل وحوادث لا أوَّلَ لها ، وقدمُ الفعلِ باطل ؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ برهان حدوثِ العالم ، والتسلسل - وهو إثباتُ حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها - باطل ، وقد سبق برهانه (۱) الثالثُ : الغرضُ : إِمَّا مصلحة في الفعل تعود إليه تعالى ، أو مصلحة تعود إلى خلقه والأوَّلُ باطل ؛ لأنَّهُ يُوجِبُ اتِّصاف ذاته بالحوادثِ ، وقد مرَّ بطلانه ، ويُوجِبُ أيضاً أن يكون ناقصاً في ذاتِهِ ، وإنما تكمل بأفعاله . والثاني باطل ؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ عدم وجوب مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح عليهِ تعالى ، ولأنَّ غرض العبد إنَّما هو حصول لذة له ، أو دفع ألم ، والله سبحانَهُ قادر على إيصال ذلك له بغيرِ واسطة فعلٍ . وأيضاً : ننقلُ الكلامَ إلى هذه المصلحة فنقول : ما الموجِبُ لخلقها ووجودها بواسطة الفعل ؟ فإن قيل : لذاتِ كونها مصلحة .. لزم تعليلُ الشيء بنفسِهِ ؛ لأنَّها صارَتْ غرض نفسها وإن قيلَ : لغرض زائدِ عليها .. نُقِلَ الكلامُ إلى ذلكَ الغرضِ ، ولزم التسلسل . 1 تعليلُ الفقهاء للأحكام بالجعل الشرعي ورعيه بالتفضل ] وكما عرفت وجوب نفي الغرض في أفعالِهِ تعالى كذلك يجب في أحكامه ، وما يذكرُهُ فقهاء أهل السنَّةِ مِنْ علل الأحكامِ إِنَّما هو بالجعْلِ
He argued in the doctrine for this claim with aspects: The first: That if He had a purpose in any of the acts, that act would be obligatory upon Him, not possible for Him to leave it. And the explanation of the entailment: That the meaning of purpose is that the act includes a wisdom that rationally impels Him to bring it about, such that His deficiency would be necessary if He did not do it. This is the meaning of purpose, so it would necessitate the act. Otherwise it would not be a purpose for which He is a cause. So my saying: (and otherwise it would not be a cause for Him) is an explanation of the entailment. And as for my saying: (so He would be coerced) it is an explanation of the second [part]; which is our saying: but the act is not obligatory upon Him, because of what follows from that of His coercion and lack of choice; for the chooser is the one from whom both act and abandonment are possible, and the assumption is that this act has a purpose with which its abandonment is not possible. And you have learned previously the necessity of His, may He be exalted, being a chooser. So it is nullified, therefore, that in any of His acts there be a purpose that impels Him to it. He said, exalted: {And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses} [Al-Qasas: 68]. The second: That the purpose: either it is eternal, then the act must be eternal, otherwise the Creator, may He be exalted, would be deficient due to the loss of His purpose; or it is originated, then this purpose needs an originated purpose, since it is among originated acts, and infinite regress and events without beginning would follow. And the eternity of the act is false, because of what you have known from the proof of the world's origination, and infinite regress — which is proving events without beginning — is false, and its proof has preceded (1). The third: The purpose: either a benefit in the act returning to Him, exalted, or a benefit returning to His creation. The first is false because it necessitates that His essence be characterized by originated things, and its falsehood has passed, and it also necessitates that He be deficient in His essence, only completing it through His acts. And the second is false because of what you have known of the non-obligation of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial upon Him, exalted, and because the purpose of the servant is only the attainment of pleasure for him, or the repulsion of pain, and God, glorified, is able to convey that to him without the intermediary of an act. And also: we transfer the discussion to this benefit and say: What necessitates its creation and existence through the act? If it is said: due to it being a benefit itself, then the thing would be caused by itself, because it became its own purpose. And if it is said: for an additional purpose beyond it, then the discussion is transferred to that purpose, and infinite regress would follow. 1 The jurists' explanation of rulings by legal stipulation and consideration by favor] And as you have known the necessity of negating purpose in His, exalted, acts, likewise it is necessary in His rulings. And what the jurists of the Ahl al-Sunnah mention of causes of rulings is only by stipulation.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage presents three proofs against the attribution of purposes (aghrad) to God's actions. The first proof argues that if God had a purpose, the act would be obligatory upon Him, contradicting His free choice. The second proof considers that if the purpose is eternal or originated, it leads to problems of temporal priority or infinite regress. The third proof divides purpose into benefit to God or to creation and shows both are false. The passage concludes by linking this to rulings: just as God's acts have no purpose, His rulings are not based on intrinsic causes but on divine stipulation.

Key Terms
الجعل الشرعي
العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Islamic rulings are based on rational purposes that obligate God.
Correction: Rulings are based on divine stipulation (جعل شرعي), not on purposes that would compel God.

Checkpoint
According to the text, how should one understand the 'causes' (علل) mentioned by Ahl al-Sunnah jurists?
A) As real efficient causes that motivate God.
B) As legal stipulations (جعل شرعي) that are merely indicators.
C) As purposes that benefit creation.
D) As eternal attributes of God.

Key Takeaway
God's rulings, like His acts, are free from purpose; juristic causes are stipulative indicators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself searching for 'good reasons' behind God's commands before you obey? What does that reveal about your view of His absolute sovereignty? Will you commit to obeying even when you see no personal benefit?
?
If God's rulings have no purpose you can grasp, does that unsettle you? Are you willing to surrender the need for explanation and submit to His will purely out of servitude?
?
When you hear a ruling you struggle with, do you secretly assume there must be a humanly appreciable wisdom behind it? Could you accept that His command is simply because He wills it, without needing to justify it to yourself?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Claim That God Acts for a Purpose
The author refutes the Mu'tazilite argument that God must act with a purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'arite school denies that God's wisdom requires a purpose for His actions, and how they define foolishness and frivolity to avoid the Mu'tazilite objection.

Core Idea
God's wisdom is His perfect knowledge and power, not acting for a purpose.

The Mu'tazilites argued that if God acted without a purpose, it would entail foolishness or frivolity, which are beneath His wisdom. The Ash'arite response, presented here by Sanusi, denies this entailment by redefining key terms. Before reading Sanusi's refutation, it helps to see how the two schools define 'purpose' and 'wisdom' differently.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite objection
The passage begins with their claim: if no purpose, then act is foolish. Sanusi then presents their full argument. Read carefully.
The objection is that foolishness and frivolity are impossible for God.
2
Analyze the definitions of safah and 'abath
Sanusi defines these terms conventionally, showing they involve ignorance or heedlessness, which cannot apply to God. Note how this breaks the supposed entailment.
This is the core of the refutation.
3
Understand Sanusi's redefinition of divine wisdom
He explains that wisdom (hikmah) for God means perfect knowledge and power, not acting for a purpose. Then he applies the same logic to divine rulings.
This completes the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : إذا لم يكن غرض فالفعل سفه
قلنا : السفه عرفاً : ما فُعِلَ معَ الجهل بالعواقب ، أو ترجيح اللذة الحاضرة ، حتى يفعل السفيه ما فيه ضرره أو حتفه وهو لا يشعرُ ، وأين هذا مِنْ فعل المتعالي عن تجدُّدِ كمال أو نقصان ، الذي لا يعزب عن علمه شيء على الإطلاق في سر وإعلان ؟!
هذهِ شبهةٌ مِنْ جهةِ المعتزلة القائلين بثبوتِ الأغراض الموجبة للأفعال والأحكام، وتقريرها أن قالوا : لو كان الفعلُ أو الحكم وقعا بغيرِ غرض لَلزِمَ السفه أو العبتُ ممَّنْ صدرا منه ، لكنَّهُ تعالى حكيم يستحيل عليه العبتُ والسفه ، فيستحيلُ إذا أنْ يفعل أو يحكم لا لغرض . والجواب : منع الملازمة ؛ وذلكَ أنَّ السفة في العُرفِ : عبارةٌ عن الجهل بالمصالح ، وخفَّةِ العقل ، حتى إنَّ السفية ليفعل ما يضر به أو يهلكه حالاً أو مالاً وهو لا يشعرُ ، أو يشعرُ للكنَّهُ لجهلِهِ وخِفَّةِ عقلِهِ يُرجحُ المرجوحَ مِنْ قضاءِ لَذَّةٍ حاليَّة لا بقاء لها مثلاً على عقوبات عظيمة دائمة
وأما العبتُ فيُطلَقُ في العرفِ : على فعل الشيء معَ الدُّهول وعدمِ القصدِ
وهذا كلُّهُ لا لزوم بينَهُ وبينَ نفْي الغرضِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : إِنَّهُ تعالى لا غرضَ له في الفعلِ ، معَ أنَّ أفعالَهُ كلَّها جاريةٌ على وَفْقِ علمِهِ وإرادتِهِ ، لا يلحقه ضررٌ مِنْ قِبَلِها ، ولا يتجدَّدُ له كمال بفعلها ، بل هو الغني في ذاتِهِ وصفاتِهِ أزلاً وفيما لا يزالُ
ثم الحكمة المنسوبة إليهِ تعالى : عبارة عن علمه بالأشياء وقدرتِهِ على إحكامها وإتقانها ، فهي تقتضي العلم والقدرة ، وهما واجبانِ لهُ تعالى ، لا فعل الشيء لغرض كما زعمت المعتزلة
وإذا فهمت هذا في أفعاله جاريةٌ على وَفْقِ علمِهِ ، لا يتطرَّقُ لَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِها نقص كيفَما وَجَّهَها على أفعاله فافهم مثله في أحكامه ؛ فإنَّها أيضاً على عبيده ، وإِنْ فسَّرَ المعتزلة السَّفَة والعبث بنفـي الغـرضِ الملازمة ، ومنعنا الاستثنائية
سلمنا
They said: If there is no purpose, then the act is foolishness. We say: Foolishness by convention: what is done with ignorance of consequences, or preference for immediate pleasure, so that the foolish person does what harms or destroys him and he does not perceive. And where is this like the act of the Exalted, who is above acquiring perfection or deficiency, from whose knowledge nothing escapes at all in secret or public? This is an objection from the Mu'tazilites, who affirm that purposes necessitate actions and rulings, and its exposition is that they said: If the action or ruling occurred without a purpose, then foolishness or frivolity would be necessary from the one who performed them, but the Exalted is Wise, and frivolity and foolishness are impossible for Him, so it is impossible for Him to act or rule without a purpose. The answer: Denial of the implication; because foolishness in convention is an expression for ignorance of benefits and lightness of intellect, so that the foolish person does what harms him or destroys him in state or property and he does not perceive, or he perceives but due to his ignorance and lightness of intellect he prefers the inferior from the judgment of an immediate pleasure that has no permanence, for example, over great lasting punishments. And as for frivolity, it is used in convention for doing something with heedlessness and lack of intention. All this has no necessary connection between it and denial of purpose because we say: He, exalted, has no purpose in the act, while all His actions proceed in accordance with His knowledge and will; no harm reaches Him from them, nor does He acquire perfection by doing them; rather He is Self-Sufficient in His essence and attributes eternally and forever. Then wisdom attributed to Him, exalted, is an expression for His knowledge of things and His power to perfect them and make them firm; so it requires knowledge and power, and both are necessary for Him, not doing a thing for a purpose as the Mu'tazilites claimed. And if you understand this in His actions proceeding according to His knowledge, no deficiency from them befalls Him no matter how He directs them, then understand the same in His rulings; for they also are upon His servants. And if the Mu'tazilites interpret foolishness and frivolity as denial of purpose, we deny the implication [of the conditional] and preclude the exclusive [conditional]. We concede.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazilite objection regarding divine purpose in actions and rulings. The author presents the objection, then provides a detailed answer. The objection states that if God's actions or rulings had no purpose, they would entail foolishness or frivolity, which are impossible for God who is Wise. The answer begins by denying the entailment. The author defines 'foolishness' (safah) conventionally as involving ignorance of consequences or preferring immediate harmful pleasure, and 'frivolity' ('abath) as doing something heedlessly without intention. These definitions rely on ignorance or lack of awareness, which cannot apply to God because He is omniscient and never unaware. Thus, there is no necessary connection between lack of purpose and foolishness/frivolity. The author then characterizes divine actions: they proceed according to God's knowledge and will, bring Him no benefit or harm, and do not add perfection. God is self-sufficient. Next, the author redefines divine wisdom (hikmah) as God's perfect knowledge and power to create things precisely, not as acting for a purpose. The passage concludes by applying this reasoning to divine rulings (ahkam) as well, and notes that if the Mu'tazilites insist on defining foolishness and frivolity simply as 'absence of purpose', the author denies the conditional implication and the exclusive conditional form of their argument.

Key Terms
غرض
سفه
عبث
حكمة
ملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's wisdom requires that He act for a purpose.
Correction: God's wisdom is His perfect knowledge and power, not acting for a purpose. Acting for a purpose implies seeking benefit or avoiding harm, which does not apply to God.

Checkpoint
Why does the author deny the Mu'tazilite claim that acting without a purpose entails foolishness or frivolity?
A) Because God can do anything, including foolish acts.
B) Because foolishness and frivolity are defined as involving ignorance or heedlessness, which are impossible for God.
C) Because the Mu'tazilites admit that God is wise and therefore must act for a purpose.
D) Because the act of God is not subject to moral categories.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'arite refutation of the Mu'tazilite argument about divine purpose hinges on redefining 'foolishness' and 'frivolity' as qualities that involve ignorance, which cannot apply to God, and redefining divine wisdom as perfect knowledge and power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial whose purpose you cannot comprehend, do you fall into the Mu'tazilite assumption that God must have a purpose you can grasp, or can you trust His wisdom as His perfect knowledge and power, even without seeing a reason? What would it take for you to truly surrender your need to know the 'why'?
?
The author redefines wisdom as God's knowledge and power, not purpose. Have you ever judged God's actions (e.g., a personal loss) as 'foolish' or 'unwise' because you could not see a purpose? How does this passage convict you of that hidden judgment?
?
If God's actions are not for a purpose but proceed from His will and knowledge, how does that challenge your tendency to evaluate His actions by human standards? Write down one area of your life where you need to stop demanding that God justify Himself to you, and commit tonight to pray for the grace to accept His wisdom without conditions.

Why Knowing Someone Can Lie Doesn't Apply to God
Sanusi answers the objection that a knowledgeable person can lie by distinguishing internal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that knowledgeable people can lie does not apply to God's speech, based on the distinction between internal and uttered speech.

Core Idea
The knowledge-bearing heart cannot lie; only uttered words can be false.

Sanusi anticipates a common objection: if we sometimes see knowledgeable people lie, why can't God lie? The answer lies in a subtle distinction. This lesson unpacks that distinction and shows why the objection misses the mark.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the passage once to see the flow: the objector raises a challenge, and Sanusi gives a precise counter-argument.
2
Identify the two types of speech
Notice the key terms: 'internal report' (khabar nafsi) and 'utterances' (alfaz). This is the pivotal distinction.
3
Understand why the heart cannot lie
Focus on the sentence: the part of the heart with knowledge cannot report a falsehood. This is the core of the answer.
The most a knower can do is 'estimate lying', not actually lie internally.
4
Connect to God's attributes
Since God is the all-knowing, His internal speech (khabar nafsi) is necessarily true. This objection does not threaten divine truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قد وجدنا العالم منا بالشيء يخبرُ عنه بالكذب . قلنا : كلامنا في الخبر النفسي ، لا في الألفاظ ؛ لاستحالة اتصافِ الباري تعالى بها ، والعالم منا بالشيء يستحيلُ أنْ يخبرَ الجزء مِنْ قلبِهِ الذي قام به العلم بخبرٍ كذب على غيرِ وَفْقِ عِلمِهِ ، غايتُهُ : أَنْ يجد في نفسِهِ تقدير الكذب ، لا الكذب
If you say: We have found the knowledgeable one among us about a thing reporting about it with a lie. We say: Our discourse is about the internal report, not about utterances; because of the impossibility of the Exalted being described by them. And the knowledgeable one among us about a thing cannot report from the part of his heart that has knowledge a false report not in accordance with his knowledge; his utmost is that he finds in himself the estimation of lying, not the lying.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector says: we see knowledgeable people sometimes lie. The answer distinguishes between internal speech (khabar nafsi) and uttered words. The argument is about God, who cannot be described by utterances; but even for humans, the part of the heart that actually has knowledge cannot produce a false report—it can only conceive of lying, not actually lie. Thus, the objection does not apply to God.

Key Terms

الألفاظ
الكذب
العلم
تقدير الكذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think that since humans sometimes lie despite knowing the truth, God could also lie.
Correction: The lying of humans is in uttered words, not in the internal speech of the heart. The heart that truly knows cannot internally report a falsehood.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's answer, why can't the knowledgeable person's heart report a lie?
A) Because God prevents it
B) Because the part of the heart that has knowledge cannot produce a false report
C) Because humans never lie
D) Because uttered words are always true

Key Takeaway
The part of the heart that knows cannot report falsely, so God's truthfulness is preserved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
God's speech is perfectly true because He is all-knowing. When you speak about Islam to others, do you speak with the same certainty that comes from true knowledge, or do you pass on what you haven't verified? What will you change today to ensure your words match your beliefs?

The Impossibility of Lying in God's Eternal Attributes
Sanusi argues that an eternal lying attribute would preclude truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the eternity of God's attributes entails the impossibility of lying in Him.

Core Idea
An eternal attribute of lying would make truthfulness impossible forever.

Sanusi presents an additional argument focusing on the eternal nature of God's attributes. If lying were an eternal attribute of God, then truthfulness could never be attributed to Him, contradicting what we know is true. This argument reinforces the divine attribute of truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: if God were described with lying, then...
2
Understand the premise
The key premise is that God's attributes are eternal. An eternal lying attribute would prevent truthfulness.
3
Connect to the conclusion
The conclusion is that lying is impossible for God because we know He is truthful. This is a logical necessity.
This argument is additional to previous ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً : لو اتَّصف البارى تعالى بالكذب ولا تكونُ صفتُه إلا قديمة .. لاستحال اتصافه بالصدقِ معَ صحة اتصافِهِ بهِ ؛ لأجلِ وجوبِ العلمِ له تعالى ، ففيه استحالةُ ما علمنا صحتَهُ
6
اعلمْ : أَنَّ دَلالة المعجزة لا يصح أن تكونَ مِنْ جملة الأدلَّةِ السمعيَّة ؛ إذ يستحيلُ أنْ تثبت صحة الأدلَّةِ السمعيّةِ قبل ثبوت دلالة المعجزة
And also: if the Exalted were described with lying, and His attribute is only eternal, it would be impossible for Him to be described with truth, in spite of the correctness of His being described with it; because of the necessity of knowledge for Him, may He be exalted. Thus there is impossibility of what we know to be correct.

Know: that the indication of the miracle cannot be from the category of revealed evidences; because it is impossible to establish the correctness of revealed evidences before the establishment of the miracle's indication.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage contains two independent points. First, an additional argument: if God could be attributed with lying, since His attributes are eternal, He could never also be truthful—yet we know He is truthful, so lying is impossible. Second, a concluding methodological remark (marked by '6') that the miracle's indication cannot itself be a revealed evidence, because that would be circular: revealed evidences depend on miracles. Therefore, the miracle's indication must be prior and independent.

Key Terms
الباري
الكذب
الصدق
القديمة
وجوب العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God could lie if He wanted, but that would contradict His nature.
Correction: The argument shows that because attributes are eternal, if lying were possible, it would make truthfulness impossible.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, why can't God be described with truth if He could be described with lying?
A) Because lying is more powerful
B) Because His attributes are eternal and thus incompatible
C) Because truth is not an attribute
D) Because knowledge is not necessary

Key Takeaway
The eternity of God's attributes means that if lying were possible, truthfulness could never be attributed to Him, so lying is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God cannot lie, how does that shape your confidence in His promises? Are there any promises from God that you doubt in your heart? What would change if you acted as if His words are absolutely certain?
?
Think of a time you told a lie. How does knowing that your Lord is eternally truthful and incapable of lying make you feel about your own deception? Will you commit to being more truthful, knowing that truth is one of His attributes?
?
The argument shows that if God could lie, truthfulness would be impossible. Apply this to your own life: if you allow even one small lie, does it poison all your speech? How can you align your speech with the attribute of truth that God possesses?

Why Miracle Indication Cannot Be from Revealed Evidences
Sanusi states that miracle indication cannot be a revealed evidence due to circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the miracle's indication must be prior to and independent of revealed evidence.

Core Idea
Miracles cannot be proven by revelation because miracles establish revelation.

Sanusi concludes his discussion on miracles with a crucial methodological point: the indication of a miracle cannot be a revealed evidence. This is because revealed evidences themselves depend on the verification of miracles to establish their truth. Thus, the miracle's indication must be established through reason prior to revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the final remark
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Note the keyword 'اعلم' (know) signaling an important point.
2
Identify the circularity
The text argues that it is impossible to establish the correctness of revealed evidences before the miracle's indication is established. This is a circular dependency.
3
Understand the implication
Therefore, the miracle's indication must come from a source other than revealed evidences, i.e., from rational proof.
This is a foundational principle in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً : لو اتَّصف البارى تعالى بالكذب ولا تكونُ صفتُه إلا قديمة .. لاستحال اتصافه بالصدقِ معَ صحة اتصافِهِ بهِ ؛ لأجلِ وجوبِ العلمِ له تعالى ، ففيه استحالةُ ما علمنا صحتَهُ
6
اعلمْ : أَنَّ دَلالة المعجزة لا يصح أن تكونَ مِنْ جملة الأدلَّةِ السمعيَّة ؛ إذ يستحيلُ أنْ تثبت صحة الأدلَّةِ السمعيّةِ قبل ثبوت دلالة المعجزة
And also: if the Exalted were described with lying, and His attribute is only eternal, it would be impossible for Him to be described with truth, in spite of the correctness of His being described with it; because of the necessity of knowledge for Him, may He be exalted. Thus there is impossibility of what we know to be correct.
6
Know: that the indication of the miracle cannot be from the category of revealed evidences; because it is impossible to establish the correctness of revealed evidences before the establishment of the miracle's indication.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage contains two independent points. First, an additional argument: if God could be attributed with lying, since His attributes are eternal, He could never also be truthful—yet we know He is truthful, so lying is impossible. Second, a concluding methodological remark (marked by '6') that the miracle's indication cannot itself be a revealed evidence, because that would be circular: revealed evidences depend on miracles. Therefore, the miracle's indication must be prior and independent.

Key Terms
الأدلة السمعية
دلالة المعجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Qur'an itself proves miracles are true.
Correction: The Qur'an is a revealed evidence; its own authenticity depends on the miracle of its inimitability, so the miracle indication must be prior.

Checkpoint

A) Because revelation is not reliable
B) Because it would be circular; revelation depends on miracles
C) Because miracles are not evidence
D) Because revealed evidences are eternal

Key Takeaway
The indication of a miracle must be established through reason before any revealed evidence can be trusted, because revelation itself relies on miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson shows that if you cannot rationally defend the miracle, your entire belief in revelation rests on shaky ground. Have you personally wrestled with this logical foundation, or have you relied on blind trust?
?
What would it mean for your faith if the miracle indication were not rationally compelling? Would you be able to justify your beliefs to a skeptic without appealing to the very scripture they doubt?

Lying is Impossible for God: Objection and Answer
Sanusi proves the impossibility of lying for God and answers the objection from human lying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why lying is impossible for God according to Sanusi, including the distinction between internal and verbal speech, and the response to the objection from human lying.

Core Idea
God's speech must conform to His knowledge; lying would negate knowledge itself.

Sanusi now tackles a critical objection: if humans can lie, why can't God? He first states the impossibility of lying for God based on the necessary conformity of His speech to His knowledge. Then he addresses the objection by distinguishing between internal report (khabar nafsi) and external words, showing that human lying pertains only to verbal expression, not to the internal act of reporting. This lesson clarifies the logical necessity of divine truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: main proof, objection, and two-part answer.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the main proof
Sanusi argues that God's report (khabar) must conform to His knowledge ('ilm). Since knowledge is necessary, the report must be truthful. If it were false, knowledge would be negated, which is impossible.
Notice the logical conditional: if lying, then knowledge absent.
3
Identify the objection
The objector points out that we see knowledgeable humans lying. This seems to challenge the claim that knowledge and truthful reporting always go together.
The objection is based on empirical observation.
4
Study the answer
Sanusi's answer has two parts: (1) The distinction between internal report (khabar nafsi) and verbal words (alfaz). God is not described by verbal speech. A knowledgeable person cannot internally report a lie; at most he can estimate a lie mentally, not actually lie. (2) If God were to lie, His attribute would be eternal, making truthfulness impossible, which contradicts what we know to be sound.
The second argument uses the eternity of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكذبُ عليهِ جلَّ وعلا محال ؛ لأنَّ خبرَهُ على وَفْقِ علمِهِ ، فيكون صدقاً ، فلو انتفى لانتفى العلم ملزومه (۱) وهو محال ؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ وجوبه . فإن قلت : قد وجدنا العالم منا بالشيء يخبرُ عنه بالكذب . قلنا : كلامنا في الخبر النفسي ، لا في الألفاظ ؛ لاستحالة اتصافِ الباري تعالى بها ، والعالم منا بالشيء يستحيلُ أنْ يخبرَ الجزء مِنْ قلبِهِ الذي قام به العلم بخبرٍ كذب على غيرِ وَفْقِ عِلمِهِ ، غايتُهُ : أَنْ يجد في نفسِهِ تقدير الكذب ، لا الكذب . وأيضاً : لو اتَّصف البارى تعالى بالكذب ولا تكونُ صفتُه إلا قديمة .. لاستحال اتصافه بالصدقِ معَ صحة اتصافِهِ بهِ ؛ لأجلِ وجوبِ العلمِ له تعالى (۲) ، ففيه استحالةُ ما علمنا صحتَهُ
Lying concerning Him, Exalted and Glorified, is impossible; because His report conforms to His knowledge, so it is truthful. So if it were absent, knowledge would be absent (its necessary concomitant) and that is impossible, due to what you have known of its necessity. If you say: We find the knowledgeable among us informing about something with a lie. We say: Our speech concerns the internal report, not the words; because it is impossible for the Exalted Deity to be described by them, and the knowledgeable among us cannot inform the part of his heart in which knowledge resides with a false report that does not conform to his knowledge. His utmost is that he finds in himself the estimation of lying, not lying itself. And also: If the Exalted Deity were described by lying, and His attribute can only be eternal, then it would be impossible for Him to be described by truthfulness while His description by it is valid, because of the necessity of knowledge for Him (Exalted). So in it is the impossibility of what we know to be sound.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a proof that lying is impossible for God, with an objection and answer. Sanusi begins by stating that lying is impossible for God because His speech (khabar) must conform to His knowledge ('ilm); thus it is true (sidq). If it did not conform, knowledge would cease to be, which is impossible given the necessity of knowledge. An objector argues that we observe knowledgeable humans lying. Sanusi answers by distinguishing between internal speech (khabar nafsi) and verbal words (alfāẓ); God is not described by verbal speech. A knowledgeable person cannot internally report a lie contrary to his knowledge; at most he can mentally estimate a lie, not actually lie. Sanusi adds a second argument: if God were described by lying, that attribute would be eternal, making it impossible for Him to be described by truthfulness, since His knowledge is necessary. Thus lying is impossible.

Key Terms
كذب
خبر نفسي
علم
صدق
قديم
حلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since humans can lie, God could also lie because He is all-powerful.
Correction: Lying is not a power but a deficiency; God's speech must conform to His perfect knowledge. The human case is only about external words, not the internal report, so the analogy fails.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is lying impossible for God?
A) Because God cannot speak.
B) Because God's speech must conform to His knowledge.
C) Because lying is a human attribute.
D) Because God has no will.

Key Takeaway
Lying is impossible for God because His speech necessarily conforms to His knowledge, and the human ability to lie only concerns external words, not the internal report.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have internal knowledge of right and wrong, yet you have spoken words that contradict that knowledge. Does that make your inner speech false as well? How does this lesson's distinction between internal and external speech expose the depth of your own hypocrisy? What will you do today to align your external words with what you truly know?
?
God's report always conforms to His knowledge. When you read the Quran, do you trust that every verse is perfectly true not just in general but specifically about you—your sins, your purpose, your end? Or do you selectively accept parts that comfort you and ignore those that demand change?
?
If it is impossible for God to lie, then everything He has promised—reward, punishment, resurrection—is absolutely certain. Are you living as if that certainty governs your daily choices? Where are you acting as if God's words might not be true?

Proof of the Impossibility of Lying for God
Sanusi presents a proof from al-Ustādh and al-Imām for God's inability to lie.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's perfect knowledge necessitates that He cannot lie, based on the proof from al-Ustādh and al-Imām.

Core Idea
God's all-encompassing knowledge makes lying impossible for Him.

This passage presents a key proof in Islamic theology demonstrating that lying is impossible for God. Building on earlier discussions, Sanusi cites a proof from two esteemed scholars, al-Ustādh and al-Imām, which links God's perfect knowledge to the impossibility of deception. The argument is concise but profound, establishing a cornerstone for understanding God's truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the definition of truthful speech.
2
Identify the key definitions
Find how the passage defines truthful speech (الخبر الصدق) and lying (الكذب). Notice that truthful speech is defined as speech matching knowledge.
3
Understand the logical link
The proof argues that God knows all things as they are, so His speech must conform to that knowledge. Why does this make lying impossible?
Consider what lying would imply about God's knowledge.
4
Recognize the implication of ignorance
Lying is defined as reporting contrary to reality. For God, such a report would only arise from ignorance. But God's knowledge encompasses all, so ignorance is impossible.
This is the crux of the proof.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The proof concludes that lying is impossible for God. Reflect on why this is necessary, not just a matter of choice.
This conclusion is foundational for understanding God's truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لمَّا كانَ هذا يتوقَّفُ على معرفة استحالة الكذب على الله تعالى . . ذكروا في بيانِ استحالتِهِ عليهِ أوجهاً أشرنا إلى بعضها في أصل العقيدة : س أحدها : للأستاذ والإمام ، قالا : كلُّ عالم في نفسِهِ حديث يطابق معلومه ، وهذا هو عين الخبر الصدقِ ، والله جل وعلا عالم بالأشياء كلها على ما هي عليه ، فيكون كلامه على وَفْقِ ذلكَ ، فاستحال عليهِ الكذبُ ؛ وهو الخبرُ عن الشيء بخلافِ ما هو عليه ؛ عليه؛ لأنَّه لا يكونُ في حقه إلا عن جهل ما هو عليه ذلك الشيء ، وذلك في حقٌّ مَنْ عمَّ علمُهُ ما لا يتناهى . . محال .
Since this depends on knowing the impossibility of lying for God Almighty... they mentioned in explaining its impossibility aspects that we indicated some of them in the original creed: one of them: from al-Ustādh and al-Imām, they said: Every knower has in himself a speech that matches his object of knowledge, and this is the very truthful report. And God, exalted and high, knows all things as they are, so His speech is in accordance with that. Thus lying is impossible for Him; and it is the report about a thing contrary to what it is; because it only occurs on His part from ignorance of what that thing is, and that is impossible for one whose knowledge encompasses the infinite.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage provides a proof for the impossibility of lying for God, building on the previous discussion. The author states that the earlier argument depends on establishing God's inability to lie. He then presents one of the proofs, attributed to al-Ustādh and al-Imām. The proof runs as follows: every knower (عالم) has within himself a 'speech' (حديث) that corresponds to his object of knowledge; this correspondence is the essence of truthful speech (الخبر الصدق). God knows all things as they truly are. Therefore, His speech necessarily conforms to His knowledge, making lying impossible. Lying is defined as reporting something contrary to its reality. For God, such a report could only arise from ignorance of the true state of affairs. But ignorance is impossible for God, whose knowledge encompasses all things without limit. Thus, God's perfect knowledge necessitates that He cannot lie. This proof grounds the impossibility of divine deception in God's omniscience.

Key Terms
استحالة الكذب
العالم
الخبر الصدق
علم الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could choose to lie if He wanted to.
Correction: The proof demonstrates that lying is impossible for God because it would stem from ignorance, which is incompatible with His omniscience. Therefore, lying is not a matter of choice but of necessity.

Checkpoint
According to the proof from al-Ustādh and al-Imām, why is lying impossible for God?
A) Because He has no need to lie
B) Because His speech must match His perfect knowledge
C) Because lying would make Him weak
D) Because prophets would then be liars

Key Takeaway
God's perfect knowledge necessitates that His speech is always truthful, making lying impossible for Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge is perfect and His speech always true, what does that mean for your own words when you claim to follow Him? Are there areas of your life where your speech does not match reality—lies, exaggerations, or omissions? What is one specific truth you have been avoiding speaking, and what would it cost you to speak it now?
?
The proof shows that lying comes from ignorance. When you lie, what ignorance are you trying to hide (fear of consequences, desire for approval, or something else)? How can you replace that ignorance with trust in God's truthfulness, knowing He never lies to you?
?
God's inability to lie means His promises are absolutely reliable. Is there a promise of God you have been doubting or treating as uncertain? What decision would you make today if you fully believed that God cannot lie and will fulfill every word He has spoken?
